Art Exhibition - 18th Day of Pre-Exhibition

Yesterday (the 25th) was the 18th day of the Shanghai pre-exhibition of the International Exhibition of Chinese Art in London. There were about 2,000 visitors, a quarter of whom were group ticket holders. Recently, many requests have been made by various schools, academic, artistic, and cultural organizations for discounted tickets and the scheduling of visits. The organizing committee is arranging dates in order of request and has already scheduled up to the 30th of this month. As the exhibition is scheduled to close on the 30th, and groups from afar are unable to come to Shanghai to visit before the closing date, they fear missing the opportunity and have requested an extension of the exhibition. The organizing committee has received many such requests recently. However, the antiquities are scheduled to be shipped to England on May 28th, and the closing process will also take time. The possibility of extending the exhibition to fulfill the hopes of those from afar is under consideration by the organizing committee. The Chinese catalogs printed by the committee have been selling very well recently, and the remaining stock is low. Negotiations are underway with the Commercial Press to reprint them. Furthermore, to ensure the timely dissemination of information, the committee contacted the local Ministry of Transportation broadcasting station yesterday to arrange for staff to broadcast news from the exhibition venue daily or every other day. This will allow those from afar who cannot visit Shanghai to understand the general condition of the exhibited antiquities. Additionally, the exhibition showcases a large number of antiquities, and visits take time. To facilitate rest for visitors, extra sofas and chairs have been placed in open spaces, along with a rest room for relaxation.

Explanation of Selected Archaeological Items

The "Explanation of Selected Archaeological Items" using oracle bones, oracle bone script, and deer head inscriptions was described in yesterday's newspaper. Here we will list the explanations for stone knives, stone axes, and hairpins: (4) Stone Knives: Stone knives were the most common daily utensils made of stone in the Yin Ruins. Over a hundred complete, undamaged examples have been unearthed, and the number of broken ones is several times greater. The stone material is mostly slate or sandstone. Ten examples with different shapes have been selected, with the first seven being relatively common and the latter seven being extremely rare, perhaps remnants of the Stone Age. (5) Stone Axes: Stone axes from the Yin Ruins can generally be divided into two categories: those with holes and those without. Each category can be further divided into several types based on their shape. It seems that only one type was commonly used, while the others may be early remnants or ritual objects used during sacrifices and dances. The six selected examples include only one that is relatively common, while the rest are unique. (6) Hairpins: Tradition holds that shapes were carved on the ends of hairpins, presumably based on some evidence. Many bone hairpins unearthed from the Yin Ruins have chicken shapes carved on them, and their shapes vary greatly. The six selected examples represent relatively common hairpin shapes, all made of bone. (To be continued tomorrow.)

Letter from Taoist Qianyin

A visitor, signing himself Qianyin Taoist, submitted a letter to the exhibition, stating his impressions: "The pre-exhibition of the London Art Exhibition has been open in Shanghai for over ten days. I was invited once and have purchased tickets myself to visit several times. I would like to share my impressions below. The arrangement of exhibits in each display room is generally in chronological order, making it easy to see the stages of evolution of our national art, which is quite scientific and commendable. Rather than calling it a 'pre-exhibition,' it would be more accurate to call it a comprehensive review of art history. Those studying art, of course, must see it, but those studying history and other social sciences must also see it. Bronzes range from the Shang and Zhou dynasties down to the Qin and Han dynasties, porcelain from the Song and Yuan dynasties down to the Ming and Qing dynasties, and embroidery also started in the Song dynasty and ended in the Qing dynasty. The closer to our era, the more exquisite, and the farther away, the more simple and crude. From an artistic point of view, although progress is slow, it is indeed moving forward. From a historical point of view, we can imagine the lives of our ancestors and the order of civilization's evolution. For example, in the bronze ware room, there is a Shang Dynasty 'Xian' (number 003) which resembles a ding tripod, with fat, hollow legs that can hold water. The upper section resembles the upper part of a ding, with a copper plate with many perforations in the middle. This copper plate can be lifted at will, presumably an ancient tool used to steam food, essentially a combination of the steamer and steaming basket we use at home today. The ingenuity of our ancestors four thousand years ago is astounding. Even today, we cannot escape the scope of our predecessors' thinking, which is both surprising and shameful. In the calligraphy and painting display room, there are many paintings but few examples of calligraphy. Over 90% are paintings. Judging from paintings alone, Tang paintings are simple and archaic, outlining contours that are as deep as carvings, which is inevitably too clear and too rigid, perhaps what is meant by 'prevailing with bone strength but not showing grace.' Song paintings gradually became more lively, with both form and spirit, endlessly varied, and far beyond what the Tang people could have imagined. The poem 'Do not belittle modern people and praise ancient people' makes sense. I have the same feeling about the paintings of the Tang and Song dynasties. Yuan paintings are increasingly refined, with all six principles reaching their peak. Ming and Qing painters, although willing to work hard, only followed in the footsteps of their predecessors, never opening up new paths, always jumping within the circle of Song and Yuan painters, and their spiritual strength feels weaker than their predecessors, with a clear downward trend. This is likely due to only knowing how to imitate and not knowing how to create. But this is based on periods. If we were to judge based on individual artists, some Ming and Qing painters can rival those of the Song and Yuan dynasties, but these are few. Based on my personal observation, if I may make a sweeping judgment, I would evaluate Chinese paintings from the Tang and Song dynasties onward as follows: from the Tang to the Yuan dynasties, painting progressed day by day, and the rate of advancement was astonishing. From the Yuan to the Qing dynasties, painting degenerated day by day, and the degree of decline was pitiful. If others don't believe me, they can spend two yuan, or one yuan if they join an academic organization, to visit the exhibition and see for themselves that my argument is not nonsense and is not without basis. The evolution and changes of Chinese characters are not found in the calligraphy and painting room, but can be glimpsed by comprehensively linking together the inscriptions on the bronze ding and yi vessels in the bronze ware room, the oracle bone inscriptions in the archaeological room, the Six Dynasties scripture writing, the few album leaves in the calligraphy and painting room, and the inscriptions on the paintings. I asked the staff why they did not collect rubbings of bronze inscriptions, famous calligraphic models, and the works of famous calligraphers of past dynasties in one room for systematic display to allow scholars of writing to study them. They replied that the exhibits were to be sent to London for exhibition. Few Westerners study Oriental writing and cannot appreciate it, so they were not selected. The ancient books listed in the ancient book display room start with Six Dynasties manuscripts and end with Qing Dynasty printed books. Looking only at the printed books, the earliest is the Five Dynasties engraved scripture discovered after the collapse of the Leifeng Pagoda. From this, one can see the stages of evolution of printing, which is that the closer to our era, the more refined. Common archaeologists and collectors always say that the older the block-printed edition, the more valuable it is, but that has a different meaning. Everyone has a different perspective, so their observations are also different. Movable type printing was first invented in our country and is called Jūzhēn edition, which our people often boast about. There are two types of Ming Dynasty movable type books on display in this room. The printing is excellent and truly rare. The Ming Dynasty woodblock printing of five-color painting manuals shows the depth of shade, and contrast of light and dark. It is unexpected that hundreds of years before the invention of five-color collotype printing, such exquisite products existed. The effort that went into them is truly astonishing. It is a pity that they are placed in glass cabinets, allowing only a glimpse and not allowing people to browse through them. In short, from this exhibition, we can see that our nation is indeed willing to work hard and is extremely intelligent. However, in certain periods, progress was very rapid, while in other periods, there was little progress, or even regression. If we can have a consistent spirit and continue to work hard, the success will not only be like this."

Municipal Tax Assessment Amount - Taxpayers Can Request Reassessment According to Regulations

The Shanghai Municipal Council announced that any taxpayer dissatisfied with the assessment amount of the municipal general tax may, within thirty days of receiving the notice of the estimated amount, fill out the form provided by the Tax Bureau (this form can be obtained from the Tax Bureau) according to the prescribed format and submit it to the Municipal Council for review. The Municipal Council will then inquire about the opinion of the Tax Assessment Committee and make a decision. If the taxpayer fails to make a statement within the time limit according to regulations, or if the statement is not successful, the estimated amount will be finalized and will not be changed.

Federation of Citizens of the Second Special District Sends Representatives to French Consul-General to Demand Six Items - Written Statements on All Points Concern the Interests of Citizens - French Consul-General Agrees to Consider and Handle After Meeting

New News Agency reports that the Federation of Citizens of the Second Special District of Shanghai in the French Concession, because the French authorities often arbitrarily search residents without following legal procedures, causing citizens to live in constant fear and anxiety, has sent a letter to Consul-General Baudrez of France requesting prompt action. The federation also elected five directors, including Mao Yun, to personally deliver the letter and request handling. Consul-General Baudrez personally received them and agreed to consider the letter and then handle it. The original text of the letter is recorded below: "Respectfully to the French Consul-General, according to a joint report from the sub-associations of the Second, Third, Fourth, Fifth, Sixth, and Eighth districts, the market has been sluggish recently, industrial and commercial enterprises have gone bankrupt, and the suffering of citizens has reached its extreme. However, the concession authorities not only do not think of remedies, but also arbitrarily increase donations, add taxes, and impose fines. If citizens do not comply slightly, they are threatened with stopping water and electricity. Furthermore, since the recovery of French rights in the Second Special District, the police have never observed the spirit of judicial independence in our country. For example, when searching residents, they have never obtained search warrants from the court, which is a serious infringement of legal rights. The members of the association have suffered unbearably and request that your consulate promptly convene a meeting to discuss remedies to reassure the citizens." After investigation, the matters mentioned by the district associations are indeed true. Therefore, the sixth plenary meeting of the directors of the association decided to propose the following points for your Consul-General to review and implement: 1. The police should obtain a search warrant from the court when searching residents. Recently, on the night of February 12, at about 8 p.m., Chinese Inspector Qian Chenglong of the police force, without a search warrant, led a large number of detectives to Wang Shunxing Wood Shop at No. 206 Pingji Road, claiming to be catching gambling. Inspector Qian Chenglong used a pistol to threaten apprentice Wang Wenqing, forcing him to confess that Dong Wenli opened a gambling den. The next day, they went to Dong's house to search and sent detectives to monitor it, falsely accusing them of gambling. This situation is extremely illegal. The details have been sent to your Consul-General for investigation and handling, but many days have passed without a reply. We request that you refer to the previous letter and handle it promptly. 2. Recently, the police have fined shops for slight non-compliance. Recently, the Yongmao Coal Shop at No. 94 Gubal Road, the warehouse at No. 106 on the same road, and the warehouses at No. 782 and 793 Julida Road were ordered to relocate within eight days and were fined 15 yuan. Since the shop's separate warehouses have not violated any regulations or engaged in illegal activities, how can they be arbitrarily fined and forced to relocate? This situation is obviously intended to disrupt business. We request that you instruct your subordinates to stop it promptly to reassure merchants and residents. 3. There are regulations for business taxes, but now the authorities arbitrarily increase donations and add taxes. If they are not satisfied slightly, they threaten to stop water and electricity. Recently, the Jusunyishi Sauce Garden at No. 187 Ximen Road had its original wine tax of 2.8 yuan increased to 7 yuan by the French Public Works Bureau in September last year. After negotiations, the chief of the bureau personally investigated and canceled the increase. The tax collector collected the accumulated original tax (2.8 yuan per month) for four months. In January of this year, the wine tax was not collected. On February 28, the bureau suddenly sent a letter stating that the monthly wine tax was set at 5 yuan, totaling 10 yuan for January and February, and demanded payment within three days, or water and electricity would be cut off. The shop refused to admit the unreasonable increase in taxes. Unexpectedly, the French Public Works Bureau cut off water and electricity on March 25. How can merchants operate under such pressure and coercion? We request that you order the bureau to cancel the increase in taxes and immediately restore water and electricity to benefit merchants. 4. Recently, bandits have been rampant, robbing in broad daylight. Recently, the Xieshunxiang Cotton Cloth Shop on Caishi Street was robbed twice, on the evening of January 13 and at 6 p.m. on the evening of March 10, suffering heavy losses. Since the shop is located in the center of the concession and the time was in the evening, the bandits dared to openly rob, which is obviously due to insufficient security. We request that you order the police to strictly pursue and arrest the bandits and add more posts in various places to strengthen security. 5. Jai alai and dog racing are disguised gambling, which harms the people through speculation. We request that you explicitly prohibit and effectively ban them to benefit the people's livelihood. 6. In the past, the concession authorities have rarely replied to official letters from this association and its district associations. We request that you instruct your subordinates to clearly reply to all past requests. The above points are all important issues that need to be resolved urgently. We have specially elected five directors, Mao Yun, Wang Shunfa, Li Weiliang, Qu Zhenhua, and Zhu Wenqi, to meet with you in person. We hope that your Consul-General will investigate and handle them, and we look forward to your reply. Sincerely, to Baudrez, French Consul-General in Shanghai."

Jiangwan Martyrs' Cemetery to Be Completed - Tomb House and Monument Completed - Memorial Archway to Be Completed in Half a Month

The Jiangwan Martyrs' Cemetery in Changgouwan Town is where the remains of military personnel and civilians who died in the Shanghai War are buried, totaling more than 1,300 bodies.

The collection and burial work was carried out by Cai Weizhang and Lu Chengyu, directors of the Jiangwan Chongshan Hall. The cost of coffins and burial was donated by Wang Weiguan, a Ningbo businessman in Shanghai. The hall then raised funds to build a monument in front of the tomb to honor the loyal souls (the construction cost was generously donated by Yan Enxiang, the former director of the Shanghai Office).

A memorial archway, a tomb house, all the above buildings were designed by engineer Quan Yuanren voluntarily. It has been a long time since the start of construction. It was originally scheduled to be completed by the end of February this year. However, due to limited funds, the progress of the project was inevitably delayed. Yesterday, a reporter from the Datong News Agency went to the Jiangwan Chongshan Hall to inquire and learned that the tomb house construction has been completed.

The construction of the monument has also been completed, and only the inscription needs to be engraved. However, the memorial archway, due to the large scale of the project, will not be completed until half a month later. The memorial inscription was written by Shen Wushi and the characters were written by Yuan Zhonglian. The full text of the

Monument Inscription is transcribed below: "On January 28, 1932, the Japanese army invaded Zhabei and attacked Wusong, exhausting all their efforts but failing to succeed. They then gathered troops in Jiangwan and ordered a general attack on January 20. In our Jiangwan territory, prosperous towns and densely populated villages were reduced to scorched earth in less than ten days. Alas, how cruel! In mid-March, the war had just ended. Cai Weizhang and Lu Chengyu, directors of Chongshan Hall, could not bear to see the bodies of anti-Japanese soldiers and fallen compatriots lying everywhere. Therefore, they organized a burial team, raised funds, selected personnel, and drew up plans, working tirelessly day and night. Even with the enemy's harsh orders and restrictions, they did not waver in their progress, exposing themselves to danger. In the winter of that year, they opened up more than nine acres of public land in Changgouwan, north of the town, and collected and buried those who had been temporarily buried in the suburbs, imitating the new European and American system, to comfort the loyal souls. Two years later, they raised funds to build a memorial archway, build a tomb house, open up thoroughfares, and decorate with flowers and trees. The entire project was completed. The sacrifices of the people in the January 28th War were great, and the survival of the nation depended on it. Only by strengthening the outlook can we inspire public will and seek to wash away the humiliation. How can we, who came after, be regarded merely as covering up bones with benevolence? In this war, 1,300 bodies were buried, not including those buried in the Guangzhao Villa. More than 15,000 yuan was spent. Yan Enbiao donated 500 yuan for the monument, and Wang Weiguan donated more than 10,000 yuan for burial expenses. Their sincerity in public welfare and their leading advocacy are admirable. The other gentlemen who contributed and donated money are not listed here for now. Respectfully written by Shen Wushi, a local resident, in the year of the Republic of China."

Young Man Commits Suicide by Jumping into the Huangpu River - Two Suicide Notes Saying He Cannot Strive - But How Does He Have the Courage to Commit Suicide?

The day before yesterday evening, after the ferry leaving the pier on Beijing Road departed, while traveling in the center of the Huangpu River, a young passenger suddenly left two suicide notes and jumped into the Huangpu River. The sailors discovered this immediately and reported it to the captain, who stopped the engine to rescue him. However, it seemed that the young man was carrying heavy objects. After entering the water, he did not surface, making rescue impossible. The captain handed the suicide notes to Xu Zhaozhen, an employee of the Municipal Ferry, who forwarded them to the Customs Water Police Station. The police found that one suicide note was addressed to his parents and the other to a friend. The words were extremely sad. They are recorded below:

(1) Dear Parents, don't be sad. Please transfer your hopes to my three younger brothers. This suicide is a last resort. I have committed such a cruel act, dying recklessly. Dad, I have harmed you. Dad, I really can't write anymore. All the words are buried in my stomach to die. If I say them, it will only make you more sad. Mom and Dad, please take care of yourselves. My younger brothers will restore the family's glory. Then I will be smiling in the afterlife. Farewell, goodbye forever. Mom and Dad, I wish you good health. Sincerely, Yun Shen.

(2) Old friend Qi, "It is better to strive to the end than to have the courage to commit suicide." These are the words we encouraged each other with. Alas, Qi, when you can't strive, what can you do? Only suicide. Old friend, don't be sad. See you in the next life. Please, Miss ×, forward my regards on my behalf. Goodbye forever, Qi, I wish you courage, Yun Shen.

After investigation by the police detectives, it was learned that the deceased was from Suzhou, 20 years old, and worked at the Shanghai Dazhong Mining Company. His colleagues did not fully understand the reason for his suicide. His friends have sent people to salvage the body, waiting for his family to arrive to collect it for burial.

Yong An Xiang Coconut Oil: Accused of Evading Taxes and Duties totaling 2,050 Gold Yuan; Defendant Claims to Have Fully Declared to Customs Broker

Yong An Xiang National Goods Store at No. 2 Tongde Lane, Zilai Street, French Concession, specializing in import and export of various goods. The main import is coconut oil produced in Singapore and other parts of Southeast Asia, shipped to Shanghai, and then distributed to other ports and inland areas. It is mainly used by various soap factories as raw material for soap production. The manager is Yong Jinqingbiao, 53 years old. Recently, the Jianghai Customs found that the store imported 200 barrels of coconut oil in January of the 21st year, with taxes and duties due totaling 2,216.28 gold yuan. Only 166.28 gold yuan were paid at the time, evading taxes and duties amounting to 2,050 gold yuan. The customs accused the store of altering the bill of lading and fraudulently taking delivery of the goods and sent a letter to the French Concession patrol for investigation. Upon receiving the letter, the patrol sent detectives on the 19th of this month to summon Jiang Qingbiao, the manager of Yong An Xiang, for investigation, and then transferred him to Criminal Court No. 8 of the Second Special District Court. After interrogation by Judge Qiu Huan Ying, it was decided that the case should be handled by the Local Court. Jiang was ordered to provide a 5,000 yuan bond, pending rescheduling and transfer to the Local Court for hearing. At 11 AM yesterday morning, Criminal Judge Wang Gangxu of Criminal Court No. 1 held a hearing. Defendant Jiang Qingbiao and his defense lawyers appeared in court. First, patrol lawyer Yuan Jiahuan presented the case, charging the defendant with forgery and fraud under Article 233 and Article 363 of the Criminal Code. Defendant Jiang Qingbiao testified that he had been the manager of Yong An Xiang for four years. Normally, the import and export tax payment procedures of the store were handled by Xin Cheng Customs Broker at No. 12 Rede Lane, Zilai Street. The merchant was unable to directly declare taxes to customs. All the coconut oil taxes and duties imported in January of the 21st year were fully paid to Xin Cheng Customs Broker for transfer to customs. Xin Cheng Customs Broker closed down in the first half of last year. He knew nothing about whether they evaded taxes or duties. After this incident, he sent a partner, Shen Qing, to find Hu Xizhuang, the manager of Xin Cheng Customs Broker, and accompanied him to the patrol, but the patrol did not interrogate him and released Hu immediately. Whether taxes and duties were evaded should be the responsibility of the customs broker. There were ledgers available to check what taxes had been paid by his store, and the ledgers had already been handed over to the patrol. Subsequently, the defendant's defense lawyers Yang Linkun, Yuan Han, and Yao Fuyuan spoke successively, stating that the French Concession patrol did not investigate or interrogate Hu Xizhuang, the key person in the case, and released him immediately. Moreover, there were witnesses to Hu's visit to the patrol. It was strange that the patrol report stated that Hu could not be summoned, and it was unknown on what grounds the accusation was made. The defendant entrusted Xin Cheng Customs Broker to handle everything at that time, and all responsibilities were borne by the customs broker. The customs also trusted the customs broker. Yong An Xiang only relied on the statements from Xin Cheng Customs Broker to pay taxes and duties, and the customs broker transferred them to customs. Now the ledgers of the defendant's store had been impounded by the patrol. Two receipts for taxes and duties paid to Xin Cheng Customs Broker could be found on the ledgers. Why didn't the patrol submit these ledgers to the court so that the facts could be clarified? The court should order the patrol to submit the ledgers to the court. At this point, the court summoned the patrol detectives in charge of the case, but neither the Chinese nor Western detectives appeared. The judge considered that the case still needed investigation, and ordered a rescheduling to the morning of the 30th for further questioning. He instructed the patrol detectives in charge to summon Hu Xizhuang for questioning at the next hearing.

Famous prostitute Hongfu Lao Jiu, on the evening of April 8th, was lured by bandit Ruan Zilin and his accomplices Lu Jianying and Li Jianguang (alias Wang) to Room 523 of the Yangtze Hotel on Yunnan Road. After being drugged and losing consciousness, they robbed her of her gold bracelet and jade ring, pawned them, and divided the proceeds before fleeing without a trace. After the prostitute regained consciousness, she reported to the patrol and requested an investigation. Detective Ruan Taibin went to Suzhou and captured Ruan. Ruan confessed that Lu and Li were hiding in Zhabei, and they were subsequently arrested. Liu Jiaji, a doctor, was falsely implicated by Ruan, who claimed that Liu had provided the drugs. As a result, Liu was also arrested. When the case was brought to the First Special District Court for investigation, Liu hired lawyer Zhang Baotang to appear in court to clarify the false accusation. The judge understood the situation and allowed Liu to be released on bail. The three defendants, Ruan, Lu, and Li, were remanded pending judgment. Yesterday morning was the date for the verdict to be announced. The patrol escorted Ruan and others to the court. Liu Jiaji, accompanied by his defense lawyer Zhang Baotang, appeared in court. Lawyer Li Zhishan, representing the patrol, also appeared in court. At 9:00 AM, Judge Jiang Shuzi took the seat in Criminal Court No. 3, briefly questioned the defendants, and then announced the verdict: Ruan Zilin was sentenced to imprisonment for four years and eight months. Lu Jianying and Li Jianguang were each sentenced to imprisonment for three years and six months. Liu Jiaji was found not guilty. After the sentencing, except for Liu who left on his own, the three convicts Ruan and others were taken back to the patrol station for detention, pending confirmation before being sent to Tilanqiao Prison to serve their sentences.

Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau's Epidemic Prevention Work to Begin on May 1st; Requesting Assistance from Concession Health Authorities; Special Agreements with Hospitals for Free Injections

Given the imminent arrival of summer, the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau deems it necessary to prepare for epidemic prevention as early as possible. A decision has been made to commence work from May 1st. Besides requesting assistance from the health authorities of the two Concessions, the Bureau is also actively preparing everything. Details are as follows:

Organizing Injection Teams: The Bureau will organize injection teams to administer vaccinations in various locations. All publicity materials related to epidemic prevention vaccinations are ready. Starting May 1st, four injection teams will be formed initially, each consisting of a doctor and a nurse. They will first go to various schools for injections, aiming to complete the work before the summer vacation. Then, they will proceed to factories, organizations, and groups for injections. From June 1st, the number of injection teams will be expanded to eight, and they will administer injections to travelers at railway stations and docks. Along the way, they will cooperate with the Public Security Bureau to enforce mandatory injections.

Special Agreements with Hospitals: To make injections accessible, the Bureau has special agreements with various hospitals to provide free injections to nearby residents. All vaccines and supplies will be provided by the Bureau. Currently, the agreed-upon hospitals include: Nanshi Public Shanghai Hospital, Southeast Hospital, Xin Pu Yu Tang Citizens' Clinic, Women and Children's Hospital, Public Education Center Clinic, Nanyang Hospital, Water God Pavilion Clinic, Taizhou Hospital, Labor Hospital, Tongde Hospital, Zhongde Hospital, Shanghai Epidemic Hospital, First Aid Epidemic Hospital, Huxi Public Clinic, Pudong Children's Clinic, Pushantang Clinic, Lianyi Society Western Hospital, Red Cross General Hospital, and the Second and Third Hospitals.

Letter to Schools: Cholera is an acute gastrointestinal infectious disease, which is extremely harmful once it becomes prevalent. Our Bureau has been providing free preventive injections for years. However, due to the large population and poor environment in this city, it cannot be eradicated in a short period of time. Now that the epidemic season is approaching, in order to prevent it, our Bureau has decided to send personnel to your school on May 1st to administer cholera preventive injections to all faculty, staff, students, and school servants, so as to prevent the disease and maintain health. A copy of the publicity material is enclosed for you to post in advance so that everyone knows about it. In addition to sending a letter to the Education Bureau to inform them, we are sending this letter to you accordingly, hoping that you will check it and act accordingly.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter to Public Works Department to Investigate and Punish Western Detective No. 122; Russian Trespasses into Pharmacy to Search Goods; Western Detective Counter-Sues Complainant for Insult

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "Dear Sirs, On the 24th of this month, according to a letter from the Shanghai New Pharmaceutical Industry Association, which quoted a letter from our member Jihuatang Pharmacy, around 3 PM on the 19th of this month, a person claiming to be a White Russian named Hekinsheng, led Chinese Constable No. 2799 to search the member's store for 'Gegelin' (轧格靈) medicine. The member at that time asked Hekinsheng if he had a search warrant from the court. He replied that he did not understand court search warrants and went to the member's storeroom without permission, forcefully taking a bundle of packaged medicines, falsely claiming that they were counterfeit Gegelin medicine. At that time, Chinese Constable No. 2799 opened and read the bundle, and it was not Gegelin, but a 'gout and bone pain relief tincture' produced by the member. Then Hekinsheng took out a bottle of Gegelin from his own bag, insisting that it was purchased from the member's store and was counterfeit. Chinese Constable No. 2799 asked Hekinsheng if he had a receipt, but he replied that he did not. The member considered Hekinsheng's actions illegal and that there were many bystanders at the door, which was detrimental to the member's reputation. Therefore, the member explained the situation to Chinese Constable No. 2799 and went together to the Lao Zha Patrol Station on Ningbo Road. Unexpectedly, Western Detective No. 122 of that patrol station, named Eynstose, listened to Hekinsheng's claim that he was American and, without asking about the facts, began to scold the member, his voice and expression were fierce, and he seemed about to use force and wanted to detain him. Fortunately, the member explained the facts to other constables and was released after a period of one and a half hours. However, Detective No. 122 never asked Hekinsheng about his nationality or investigated the member's donations and taxes, which were supposed to protect his peace and security. This Western detective, being paid by the public, did not use legal procedures and treated the member in this way, which is extremely detrimental to the reputation of a fair agency and damages the interests of the member. This is not only the damage suffered by the member alone, so we are sending this letter to your council, requesting that you forward it to the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, requesting that you give the Western Detective appropriate punishment, etc." Upon receipt, it was found that Hekinsheng had entered the store without a court search warrant and searched the items without permission, which was already illegal. The Western Detective, without asking about the truth of the facts, added insults, which was an abuse of power and should be thoroughly investigated. Therefore, we are sending a special letter to your council, requesting that you forward it to the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, requesting that you thoroughly investigate the truth and strictly punish him, which is our earnest hope. Upon receipt, it was found that since Hekinsheng did not carry a search warrant, there was no way to prove that his search was due to the performance of his duties. The Jihuatang Pharmacy stopped him and invited Chinese Constable No. 2799, who witnessed the scene, to the Lao Zha Patrol Station to inquire about the truth, which was a necessary measure to protect the safety of the business. Western Detective No. 122, as a public official, should have had rules for handling affairs. A citizen making a complaint to a public official is not a crime. Insulting a citizen's personality is a minor offense, and such an impression left in the minds of the general public would further damage the relationship between China and foreign countries. Since our council has received a report from the association, we are sending a letter to your bureau accordingly, and we hope that you will give a fair and just disposition, which is our earnest request."

New Shanghai-Taicang Automobile Station Completed; Scheduled to Move into New Station on May 1st

The Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Company began preparations in a flat in the intersection of Gonghe New Road and Yongxing Road in Zhabei in 1920. It opened to traffic in 1921, initially only reaching Dachang, gradually extending to Liuhang and Luodian. On New Year's Day of 1922, the entire route was opened to traffic. At the same time, a ticket office was built at the intersection of Zhongxing Road and Gonghe New Road, which is now Ding Huai Detang Pharmacy. Later, as business became increasingly developed, a larger Shanghai station ticket office was built at the intersection of Datong Road and Baoshan County Road (now Shanghai-Taicang Road) in 1928. Various offices were attached to it. Currently, in order to facilitate passengers, the station has rented land at the intersection of Guangfu Road and Wu Bo Road Bridge and built a new three-story Western-style building. It is now completed. The lower floor is the waiting room, ticket office, stationmaster's office, etc. The second floor is the offices of various departments, and the third floor is the dormitory. The back is the garage, where passengers can get on and off the bus. There are several small rooms for tea porters, etc. It is also understood that the company's fares will not increase. In addition, the Wu Zhen Road Bridge to the original station will not stop. Non-company employees are not allowed to get on and off the bus because that section is the business scope of the Chinese public bus and there is a contract.

Land Bureau Announces Regulations for Church Land Leases; After the Church and Lessor Inspect Ownership Certificates Together, the Bureau Approves and Issues the Lease in the Prescribed Form

The Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau issued Bulletin No. 177 yesterday, ordering compliance with the Rules for Land Leases by Foreign Churches, in accordance with instructions. The bulletin and regulations are recorded below:

The Land Bureau issued Bulletin No. 177 yesterday, stating: "According to Order No. 12412 from the Shanghai Municipal Government, 'After investigating a dispatch from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Interior stating that a dispatch from your Municipal Government No. 859 on January 24 of the twelfth year, enclosing a copy of the Rules for Land Leases by Foreign Churches Issued by the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau and a sample lease, has been received and requested for verification and joint handling, etc., has been received by the Ministry and thoroughly reviewed, and after repeated consultations, it has been deemed appropriate. In addition to filing for record, a corresponding reply is hereby given for your reference and handling, etc.,' has been received. In light of this, and given that the Bureau had previously submitted a request for expedited action, it is hereby ordered that the Bureau immediately comply with and implement the attached Rules for Land Leases by Foreign Churches Issued by the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau and publish them for public knowledge. This Bulletin."

Rules: Rules for Land Leases by Foreign Churches Issued by the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau. Article 1: Any foreign church that establishes a church hospital or school in this city that is permitted by the treaty between that country and China may lease land in the name of the church. Article 2: Any foreign church leasing land in this city shall comply with the Regulations on Land and Housing Leases by Foreign Churches in the Interior promulgated by the National Government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs, as well as the provisions listed in these Rules. Article 3: Any foreign church leasing land in this city must jointly submit to the Bureau, together with the lessor, the ownership certificate and clarify the following items for the Bureau's review: (1) Agreement on the lease term; (2) Location and area of the land; size and style of the house; (3) Use of the land and house within the scope of the church's purpose; (4) Nationality of the church; (5) Lease term, total amount of rent. Article 4: After the land lease is approved by the Bureau, the Bureau shall notify the lessor and the lessee church to come to the Bureau to sign the land lease. After both parties sign or seal the lease, it will be issued to both parties for safekeeping as evidence. The original ownership certificate will be returned to the lessor for safekeeping. Article 5: The form of this land lease will be prescribed separately and issued by the Bureau. Each lease shall consist of three identical copies, with the first copy given to the lessee church, the second copy given to the lessor, and the third copy kept by the Bureau for record. Article 6: After the land lease contract is established, the lessee church shall pay the registration fee, which shall be calculated at a rate of one percent of the total rent, and both parties shall pay a lease fee of one yuan each. Article 7: If the lease term expires and the lessee wishes to continue the lease, they must jointly submit to the Bureau for review in accordance with Article 3 of these Rules after obtaining the consent of the lessor. Article 8: These Rules may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered. Article 9: These Rules shall come into effect on the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Misfortunes in "Manure King's" Family: Another Lawsuit Arises; Concubine of Hong Kui Files Suit; Requesting Recognition of Status

Following the death of Ma Fuqi, the late "Manure King," and his wife, A'gui Jie's eldest son, Ma Hongkui, in the autumn of last year due to illness, Ma Chen, Hongkui's wife, along with her children, Ma Lusheng, Luying, and Luzhen, hired lawyers and sued Ma Honggen, her husband's younger brother, and Ma Wang, her husband's concubine (also known as Wang A'da), in the Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court, for encroaching on inheritance. The court has repeatedly held hearings and summonsed parties, but postponed the hearing and ordered the parties to hire accountants to verify the property and reach a settlement. Details have been previously reported. Now, Ma Qin (24 years old), a woman from Nanjing and the concubine of the late Ma Fenghui, together with her son, Lushan (11 years old), hired lawyers and filed a petition in the Civil Court of the First Special District Court against Ma Chen and her children, requesting mediation and recognition of her status. The petition states that Ma Hongkui, the late husband of Ma Chen, had a relationship with the petitioner in 1923. The following year, they cohabited in Yongfu Lane on Lanweiai Road and later gave birth to a son, Lushan. At the time, Hongkui's mother, A'gui Jie, learned of the situation and was delighted to have a grandson. She ordered Honggen to move the petitioner to a house built by her in Guifu Lane, Beile Road, to save expenses. Soon after, Hongkui's father, Fuqi Gong, passed away. The petitioner and her son also went to the house to mourn and wear mourning clothes. During the seven-day memorial, Lushan's name was included in the funeral oration. Later, Hongkui took Wang A'da as a concubine, and as a result, his affection for the petitioner gradually faded. The petitioner, unable to support herself, took her son to work for a living. Recently, the petitioner learned of Hongkui's death, and her future life became even more difficult. She also resents that she has not been recognized for more than ten years. Therefore, she requested that the defendants be summoned to court for mediation and recognition of her status. The court approved the petition and summoned both parties, scheduling the hearing for mediation yesterday morning. However, the bailiffs went to the residences of the defendants, Ma Chen and others, at No. 11 Guifu Lane on Boer Road and No. 183 on Wilmont Road, to serve the summons, but because Ma Chen and her children had moved away after becoming involved in the lawsuit with Honggen and others, their addresses were unknown, and the summons could not be served. At 10:20 AM yesterday, Judge Ma Yishu of the Second Special District Court mediated the case in Civil Court No. 7. None of the defendants appeared in court. The petitioner Ma Qin and her son Ma Lushan were also represented by their lawyers. The judge stated that the addresses of the defendants were unknown, and the summons could not be served. Therefore, the court could not proceed with the mediation, and the mediation was deemed unsuccessful. The petitioner could file a formal lawsuit separately. If the defendants' addresses were still unknown and the summons could not be served at that time, it could be served by public notice. After the announcement, the court adjourned.

Purchasers of Real Estate in Fuxing Village Petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau the Day Before Yesterday; The Bureau Scheduled a Three-Party Mediation

Dagong News: Purchasers of real estate in Fuxing Village, Xiangshan Road, Zhabei, because of the long-standing dispute over the mortgage of the land, which is likely to harm the interests of the purchasers, decided to organize a petition. Yesterday, they petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau. It was learned that Youji Company was jointly operated by Chen Changkun, Hu Qihui, Guo Weichen, Liu Hengfu, etc. After the January 28th Incident, they mortgaged the land at the corner of Xiangshan Road and Shichang Road (now Fuxing Village), about eleven mu, to Wang Weiguan, the owner of Delong Tobacco Company, for 125,000 yuan. Later, Hu and Wu withdrew and merged into Chen Changkun alone, renamed Renji Company. Chen, due to lack of funds, was unable to repay the mortgage when it was due and was sued by Wang. Chen, without waiting for the end of the lawsuit, planned to build more than 100 houses on the original site in June of last year, each house and land priced at 2,000 to 2,500 yuan, and set a payment method in installments, selling them piecemeal. Advertisements were placed in newspapers. The general public, unaware of the dispute, purchased 144 houses. Of these, 80 houses were completed by the end of last year, and about 60 households had already moved in. Now, because the creditor Wang Weiguan hired lawyer Wang Youling to file a lawsuit in court for execution, the purchasers believed that it was related to their own interests and negotiated with Chen and Wang, but with no results. Therefore, they organized a joint association of purchasers. In addition to electing Xu Chuanxian as a representative to petition the Municipal Party Department on the 22nd of this month, they also organized a petition group, with more than 60 participants, to petition the Social Affairs Bureau on the afternoon of the 24th, and put forward four petition objectives. The director of the Public Welfare Section of the Fourth Section of the Bureau received them, and the petition representatives personally explained the suffering of being deceived by land traffickers and coerced by wealthy people. Director Sun expressed deep sympathy for the matter, which concerned the livelihood of the majority of the people, and promised to convene a three-party mediation to protect the rights of each purchaser. The representatives then left.

Deported Overseas Chinese from Japan: Fiftieth Batch Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday; Yang Zongxing and Three Others Return to Their Hometowns by Boat That Evening

The fiftieth batch of deported overseas Chinese from Japan, including Yang Zongxing, Wang Ayuan, Qiu Risheng, and Chen Baoxiang, natives of Wenzhou, Zhejiang Province, arrived in Shanghai at 3:00 PM yesterday aboard the Japanese vessel "Rokko Maru." The ship was originally scheduled to arrive the day before yesterday but was delayed due to fog en route. After disembarking, these distressed overseas Chinese originally intended to petition the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, but due to insufficient travel funds and fearing greater financial difficulties if they stayed in Shanghai longer, they immediately transferred to a boat that evening to return to their hometown of Wenzhou.

Jiangsu Province Purchases 100,000 Sheets of Silkworm Eggs from Japan; 3,000 Sheets Have Been Shipped to Shanghai and Transferred to Wuxi; The Rest Will Arrive Successively

Due to the silkworm breeding farms having already shipped silkworm eggs to Zhejiang for sale, Jiangsu Province is experiencing a shortage of silkworm eggs for the spring season. With the silkworm rearing season approaching, the existing silkworm egg sales outlets in various locations are facing a situation where demand exceeds supply, and all silkworm eggs have been sold out. To alleviate the silkworm egg shortage, the Wuxi Provincial Silkworm Experiment Station and the Silkworm Model Area have submitted a request to the provincial government to purchase silkworm eggs from Japan and have reached an agreement with Mr. Jinzi, a Japanese silkworm egg merchant in Shanghai. Other locations, such as Shanghai, Suzhou, Baoying, and Nanjing, are also purchasing silkworm eggs from Japan, totaling 100,000 sheets. The selling price is one yuan per sheet. The first batch of 3,000 sheets has been shipped from Japan to Shanghai and transferred to Wuxi. The remaining batches are expected to arrive within the next few days.

Huangmei County in Hubei Province suffered the most severe disaster last year, with tens of thousands of people dying. The spring famine has left people starving. Although your association allocated 2,000 piculs of rice to Shanghai for disaster relief in January and February of this year, it only reached 10,000 elderly, weak, and impoverished people. The remaining tens of thousands of disaster victims are on the verge of starvation at this time of year when food supplies are scarce. Please urgently telegraph your association to find a way to provide assistance. Our county suffered a severe disaster, which your esteemed association has already understood, so we will not repeat the details. Now, at a time when people are starving due to the spring famine, and when the communists are pressing on the border, the local situation is precarious, and the people's lives are in imminent danger. We earnestly request your association to quickly allocate a large sum of money to provide relief so as to prevent tens of thousands of disaster victims without clothing or food from becoming displaced and being exploited by the communists. This would be fortunate. Urgent appeal, with utmost sincerity. Wu Xingya bows respectfully."

Progress is very slow, and wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in Shanghai reached a high of 81.5 and a low of 56.7. Letter

To the Editor: I am writing to you regarding the news item in today's news column about the closure of the Huaming Silver Bank. The facts are slightly inaccurate, and the names of the shareholders and managers are mostly speculative and untrue. The manager of the Huaming Silver Bank is Mr. Shen Nianzu, who has had significant dealings with various sectors, with substantial inflows and outflows, and has a strong reputation for creditworthiness. Currently, due to the inability to collect loans on time, it has temporarily suspended operations and is working hard to remedy the situation. There may be hope for resumption of business. Before reaching the liquidation stage, our firm and Mr. Wang Sifang, the certified accountant, are only representing the notification of the suspension of operations, pending a resolution. Who the shareholders are is not something that can be discussed at this time, so there is no such thing as keeping secrets. Fearing that the outside world will misunderstand the truth and spread rumors, I am writing to request a correction. Sincerely, Lai Shi Hong Shihao, 25th.

Widow Sues Aunt Seeking Division of Property; Aunt First Files Lawsuit to Confirm Guardianship; Court Orders Both Parties to Attempt Mediation; If Unsuccessful, Further Hearing Will Be Held

Sun Jianquan, a wealthy merchant from Ningbo residing in Shanghai, passed away due to illness in March of this year at No. 61, Taihe Lane, Huade Road. He left behind an elderly wife, Mrs. Wang, who is in her seventies, and five grandchildren. Besides the eldest granddaughter, Maiyu, who has married and lives separately with her husband, Mr. Zhu, at No. 57, Taihe Lane, the second granddaughter, Maidi, was taken away by the widow, Li Yuegui, to raise. The remaining three grandchildren are all young and are being taught at home by a tutor hired by Mrs. Wang, allowing her to enjoy

the joy of being with her grandchildren.

However, recently, because her widowed daughter-in-law, Li Yuegui, left the family six or seven years ago and even published a statement in the newspaper stating that she intended to remarry, the family requested that Baodi be returned. But Li Yuegui firmly refused. Thereupon, Sun Wang retained lawyer E Sen and filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Local Court seeking confirmation of her right to guardianship over her granddaughter, Baodi. Li Yuegui, on the other hand, claiming that her father-in-law Sun Jianquan's entire estate was no less than 200,000 yuan, and knowing that it was now under her aunt's control, also retained a lawyer in her capacity as the legal representative of her daughter Baodi to file a lawsuit against Sun Wang,

seeking a division of the estate.

She claimed that the estate was estimated to be worth 200,000 yuan. Besides her aunt, Sun Wang, who should receive half, the remainder should be divided into six shares for the five children of her deceased husband, Sun Tongqing, and herself, so that she and her daughter can maintain their livelihood. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiao Wanxuan held a hearing on the case filed by Sun Wang seeking confirmation of guardianship. Because the defendant, Li Yuegui, failed to appear, Judge Qiao only questioned the plaintiff, Sun Wang, briefly and adjourned the hearing. Afterwards, Judge Zhang Qinglan held a hearing on the property division case. Li Yuegui, being the plaintiff, brought her fourteen-year-old

daughter Baodi

to court. She testified that she was 35 years old and currently lived at No. 6, Shangqin Lane, Qingdao Road, supporting herself and her daughter through handicrafts. She had married Sun Tongqing, the son of the defendant Sun Wang, at the age of 21 as a second wife. His first wife was originally her elder sister, who had two daughters. After her sister died, Tongqing married her as a second wife. She gave birth to two daughters and a son. In 1925, her husband died of illness. Since then, she has been subjected to abuse by the defendant, even falsely accusing her of having

an affair

with her father-in-law. When she was 28 years old, her mother fell ill, but she was not allowed to return to her home province. The various instances of abuse were difficult to describe. She attempted suicide once that year but was rescued. She reluctantly survived until the following year, at the age of 29, when she felt she could no longer live there and took her daughter Baodi and left home. Originally, she intended to commit suicide again, but because she worried that no one would raise this daughter, she continued to live. The defendant once told her that her father-in-law's entire estate was worth 200,000 yuan. She now specially requests a legal division of the estate. While speaking,

tears welled up in her eyes.

Then, lawyer E Sen, representing the defendant Sun Wang, presented a newspaper to the court, stating that Li Yuegui had engaged a lawyer in 1930 to publish a statement in the newspaper declaring her departure from the defendant's family and indicating her intention to remarry. Baodi was born to the defendant's son Tongqing. Because Li Yuegui had made this intention clear, the defendant requested that she return Baodi so that she could receive the same education as the other grandchildren. This is why she filed the lawsuit seeking confirmation of guardianship. The case has already been heard, but because Li Yuegui did not appear, the hearing was adjourned to May 4th for a retrial. Li Yuegui,

after her aunt filed the lawsuit,

also filed a lawsuit seeking a division of property. Since she had published a statement in the newspaper a few years ago declaring her intention to remarry, her current claim for a division of property is obviously intentional. Therefore, the court should suspend this case temporarily and wait for a ruling on the guardianship case before proceeding with the review. Otherwise, the hearing of this case would be hindered. Upon hearing this, Li Yuegui quickly stated that the newspaper statement was merely an expression of intention and that she

had not remarried.

The court then summoned the defendant Sun Wang for questioning. Although she was already in her seventies, she was vigorous, sharp-eared, clear-eyed, and spoke with a clear voice, appearing as if she were only in her fifties. According to her statement, Li Yuegui was formerly her daughter-in-law, but she has been away for several years. Even if she has not openly remarried, she likely has a lover. But her granddaughter was born to her son, so she should be asked to return her so that she can receive the same education as her other grandchildren. Judge Zhang then ordered the parties to leave and attempt mediation. If unsuccessful, a further hearing will be held.

Educational News

Ministry of Education Issues Order on New Enrollment Methods for Universities: Enrollment Must First Explain the Situation of Faculty and Facilities

(Nanjing, 25th) The Ministry of Education has newly established enrollment methods for universities and has issued an order for their implementation. The purpose is, on the one hand, to adapt to national needs, and on the other hand, to seek practical teaching efficiency. Therefore, the new methods stipulate that all departments should be carefully reviewed by each school regarding the situation of faculty and facilities, and the number of students enrolled in each department should be determined to be in line with the actual situation of each department, so as to achieve the effect of focused attention and earnest education. Regarding the departments of literature, law, and business education, according to the enrollment statistics of each school last year, the average number of students in each department of the School of Literature was sixteen, in each department of the School of Law was twenty-seven, in each department of the School of Business was twenty-two, and in each department of the School of Education was fifteen. In the new methods, for the enrollment of these departments, except for those with outstanding achievements who have been specially approved by the Ministry before enrollment, all are limited to thirty, and no excessive enrollment is allowed. In the display of tolerance, there is also the meaning of restriction and considerable compression. Moreover, the enrollment situation of each school has generally become stable. Therefore, after the new methods are established this year, if there are no special circumstances in the coming years, they will be handled according to these methods. The five articles of the methods are as follows: 1. All departments of literature, law, business, education, science, agriculture, medicine, and engineering under each university and independent college shall, in the future, carefully review the faculty situation and facilities of each department when enrolling new students and transfer students, and determine the number of students enrolled in each department in order to actually obtain teaching efficiency and shall not allow excessive enrollment. 2. Universities with Schools of Literature, Law, and Business Education, etc., and independent colleges with departments of Literature, Law, and Business Education, etc., shall, according to the statistics of enrollment of each school in the 23rd year of the Republic of China, the average number of new students and transfer students enrolled in each department of each school or department shall be approximately twenty. In the future, the number of new students and transfer students enrolled in each department or specialized subject of each school or department shall be limited to thirty, except for those with particularly excellent achievements who have been specially approved by the Ministry before the examination. Universities with Schools of Science and Literature or independent colleges with departments of Science and Literature shall follow the provisions of the preceding paragraph for the enrollment of new students and transfer students in each department or specialized subject of each school or department that belongs to literature, law, and business education. Universities with Schools of Science, Agriculture, Engineering, and Medicine or independent colleges with departments of Science, Agriculture, Engineering, and Medicine, etc., shall also follow the provisions of this article for the enrollment methods of departments or specialized subjects of literature, law, and business education, etc., if they are attached to them. 3. The Ministry will not approve the entry qualifications of new students and transfer students of schools that enroll students in accordance with these methods. 4. These methods shall be implemented from the summer vacation of the 24th year of the Republic of China. 5. These methods do not apply to colleges that only accept female students for the time being.

Guangdong Province: Promotion of Normal and Vocational Education

The Department of Education of Guangdong Province recently proposed measures to promote normal education and vocational education, which were submitted to the Provincial Government for resolution and amendment. The summary is recorded below:

(A) "Normal Education" In accordance with Article 10 of the Ministry of Education's Normal School Regulations and in consideration of local conditions, the province is divided into ten normal school districts, and one normal school and one normal school for girls are established in each district. (1) The Guangzhou District includes thirteen counties. There were originally one normal school and one normal school for girls. The boys' school was renamed the Provincial Jiangcun Normal School, and the girls' school was renamed the Provincial Guangzhou Normal School for Girls. (2) The Huizhou District includes eight counties. There was originally no provincial normal school. A normal school was added in Laolong, Longchuan County, within the district, named Laolong Normal School. (3) The Chaoshan District includes twelve counties. The original Second Normal School was renamed the Provincial Hanshan Normal School. (4) The Meizhou District includes five counties. There was no normal school. A Lizining Normal School was established in Xingning County, within the district. (5) The Nan Shaolian District includes eleven counties. The original Third Normal School was renamed the Provincial Shaozhou Normal School. (6) The Zhao Luo District includes eleven counties. The original Fourth Normal School was renamed the Provincial ______ Normal School. (7) The Wuyi Liangyang District includes eight counties. There was no normal school. The Provincial Changsha Normal School was established in Changsha, Kaiping County, within the district. (8) The Gao Lei District includes nine counties. The original Fifth Normal School had previously been changed to the First Agricultural School. The original Provincial Tenth Middle School in the district will be changed to a normal school, called the Provincial ______ Zhou Normal School. (9) The Qinlian District includes four counties. There is no normal school in the district. There are two middle schools. The original Twelfth Middle School will be changed to a normal school, called the Provincial Qinzhou Normal School. (10) The ______ Yai District includes thirteen counties. The original Sixth Normal School was renamed the Qiongyai Normal School. (Explanation) Normal schools have been established in the five districts of Guangchao, Nan, Zhao, and Qiong. Guangzhou also has a normal school for girls. Those that have not been established are the five districts of Hui, Mei, Wu, Gao, and Qin. In addition to changing the original middle schools in the two districts of Gao and Qin, three more normal schools should be added. These three schools should be established in stages in consideration of the needs of small schools and teachers and the situation of education fees in each district. For girls' normal schools in each district, Guangzhou has already been established. It is planned to simultaneously select locations to establish schools in the two districts of Chao and Gao. For the remaining districts, it is planned to complete the establishment of normal schools in each district three years later, and then plan in accordance with the regulations.

(B) "Vocational Education" Provincial vocational schools will be planned and established annually in accordance with the normal school districts and considering the situation in various places. (1) The Guangzhou District will expand the original Provincial First Vocational School and rename it the Provincial Guangzhou Agricultural and Industrial Vocational School. The original Second Agricultural School will be renamed the Provincial Shunde Agricultural Vocational School. In Guangzhou, one Provincial Commercial Vocational School and one Provincial Girls' Domestic Affairs Vocational School will be established. (2) There is currently no vocational school in the Huizhou District. It is planned to establish a Provincial Agricultural Vocational School in Heyuan County to run horticulture and agricultural product manufacturing departments, named the Provincial Heyuan Agricultural Vocational School. (3) There is currently one Provincial Lingdong Commercial Vocational School in the Chaoshan District, which will be expanded. An industrial vocational school will be established in Chao'an in the district to run a ceramics department, named the Provincial Chao'an Industrial Vocational School. (4) The Meizhou District currently has the Third Agricultural School, which will be expanded and renamed the Provincial Meizhou Agricultural Vocational School. A Provincial Xingning Industrial Vocational School will also be established in Xingning. (5) There is currently no vocational school in the Nan Shaolian District. A Provincial Yunzhou Agricultural Vocational School will be established in Yingde to run forestry and horticulture departments. (6) There is currently no vocational school in the Zhao Pan District. A Provincial Sihui Agricultural Vocational School will be established in Sihui to run forestry and agricultural product manufacturing departments. (7) There is currently no vocational school in the Wuyi Liangyang District. A Provincial Jiangmen Agricultural Vocational School will be established in Jiangmen to run horticulture and agricultural product manufacturing departments. (8) The Gao Lei District currently has the First Agricultural School, which will be expanded and renamed the Provincial Gaozhou Agricultural Vocational School. A fisheries vocational school will also be established in Leizhou, named the Provincial Leizhou Fisheries Vocational School. (9) There is currently no provincial vocational school in the Qinlian District. A Provincial Qinzhou Industrial Vocational School will be established in Qinzhou to run ceramics and simple chemical industries. (10) There is currently no vocational school in the Qiongyai District. A Provincial Nada Agricultural Vocational School will be established in Nada, Yan County, to run forestry, animal husbandry, horticulture, and agricultural product manufacturing departments. (Explanation) There are already three provincial agricultural schools, one industrial school, and one commercial school. It is planned to add six agricultural schools, three industrial schools, one commercial school, and one domestic affairs school. The departments that should be run by vocational schools in a certain district in the 23rd to 26th years should be determined at any time based on investigations and consideration of the situation in each district. According to the regulations on vocational schools, primary schools should be established by counties and cities as a general rule, and senior schools should be established by the province as a general rule. However, there are no regulations on running senior schools because vocational education in various counties and cities is still underdeveloped. At present, provincial vocational schools should still first run primary schools or run both senior and primary schools concurrently.

Japan Suddenly Convenes the Pan-Pacific Education Conference, Initiated by the Japan New Education Association

(World News Agency, Tokyo) The Japan New Education Association, in order to promote Japanese culture, has initiated the convocation of the Pan-Pacific Education Conference. The Ministry of Education, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Railways, the International Culture Promotion Association, the Imperial Education Association, and the Japan-America Association have all provided strong support. It has been decided to hold the conference from August 1st to 8th in the Central Lecture Hall of Tokyo University. The Association has issued 2,500 invitations to the education directors of cities in Pacific countries. It is predicted that about 300 educators from Japan and about 200 from various countries will participate in the conference. The Japanese side attaches great importance to this conference and has decided to have specialized scholars lecture on the Imperial Rescript on Education made by Emperor Meiji, Japanese art, and the Japanese education system. It is scheduled that Dr. Taki Seiichi will lecture on Japanese art, and Dr. Yoshida Kumaji will lecture on the Meiji Rescript and the education system. The topics of the conference will be divided into 21 categories, including various types of education from elementary school to university, social education, family education, new educational philosophy, overseas education, rural education, psychology and new education, and the education of educators.

Citywide Boy Scouts to Hold Inspection and Camping Tomorrow, Divided into Six Districts to be Held Separately, All Measures Have Been Drafted

The Boy Scout movement in this city has been vigorously developed in recent years under the advocacy of the government and the support of the community. Recently, the number of Boy Scout troops registered and being registered in the city has reached more than 130, and many schools and social groups have also begun to organize. The Boy Scout Council of this city will assess the past training achievements of various Boy Scout troops to serve as a reference for improving work, in order to seek the historical expansion of the Boy Scout movement in this city, and will hold the sixth citywide Boy Scout inspection and camping. The city is divided into six districts, which will be held separately in each district. After several meetings, various items have been determined, and the funding has been determined. The dates, locations, and methods of each district are as follows:

Dates and Locations The first district is the entire Pudong area, on May 4th and 5th, at the Peidong Yangjing Sports Field. The second district is Nanshi and part of the First and Second Special Districts, on April 26th, 27th, and 28th, at Wu Jia Hang. The third district is the First Special District, on June 1st, 2nd, and 3rd, at the Jiangwan Qujiaqiao Sincere Sports Field. The fourth district is the city center area, part of Jiangwan, Wusong, and Zhabei, on May 11th, 12th, and 13th, in front of the Municipal Government. The fifth district is Huxi, part of the Second Special District, on May 17th, 18th, and 19th, at the Daxia University on Zhongshan Road. The sixth district is Zhenru, part of the First Special District, and part of Zhabei, on May 17th, 18th, and 19th, at the Daxia University on Zhongshan Road.

Inspection Methods The methods for the Shanghai City District Inspection and Camping of the Chinese Boy Scouts (Article 1) The district inspection and camping shall be presided over by the district instructor and assisted by the Shanghai Special City Council of the Chinese Boy Scouts (hereinafter referred to as the Council). (Article 2) The district inspection and camping shall be held after the Council makes a decision, notifies the districts, and the districts determine the date and location and report to the Council for approval. (Article 3) The funding for the district inspection and camping shall be subsidized by the Council according to the situation in each district. (Article 4) During the district inspection and camping, each Boy Scout troop under each district must have at least 18 members participate. (Article 5) During the district inspection and camping, each district must follow the "Shanghai City Boy Scout Curriculum Competition Rules" established by the Council to hold curriculum competitions. (Article 6) During the district inspection and camping, each district may set up an office, with the director and deputy director of each district serving as the director and deputy director of the office, and establish four sections: inspection, camping, competition, and general affairs, each with one chief and several staff members, all of whom shall be hired by the district instructor. (Article 7) The performance evaluation and curriculum competition judging matters of the district inspection and camping shall be handled by the personnel hired by each district. (Article 8) The inspection personnel of the district inspection shall be invited by the Council. (Article 9) The order of the inspection ceremony, the procedure of action, and the camping schedule and rest time of the district inspection and camping shall be formulated by the office of each district and reported to the Council for record in advance. (Article 10) If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, the Council shall revise them at any time.

Around the World by Bicycle from Florida, Indian Boy Scout Mody Arrives in Shanghai, Visits the Boy Scout Council of this City Yesterday, Boy Scout Council Hosts Tea Party to Welcome Him

Indian Rover Scout J.R. Mody, just nineteen years old, is adventurous and represented Bombay, India at the World Boy Scout Jamboree in Australia last year. He is skilled in cycling and can perform for 24 hours at a time without eating or resting. Mody departed from Bombay on May 6th last year, making a grand tour of the world by bicycle. Wherever he could travel by bicycle, he drove forward. It has been almost a year since then, having traveled thousands of miles. Recently, he arrived in Shanghai from Australia via Hong Kong and is currently staying at 120 Renji Road. Mody visited the Boy Scout Council of this city at 10:00 a.m. yesterday. The managing director Qu Yue, directors Luo Lie, Wang Gang, Sun Yixin, and all the staff held a tea party to entertain him. During the meeting, they presented him with the General Badge of the Chinese Boy Scouts and various publications of the Council. It is reported that Mody will take a bicycle to Beijing within days, then go north to Pingjin, and then to Dalian, pass through Seoul and reach Busan, then cross the sea to Japan, and take the route through Europe and America, through Africa, Arabia, Persia, and Afghanistan to return to his hometown. It is estimated that it will take another three years to complete the entire journey.

Secondary School Normal School Education Research Conference, Held a Teacher Research Conference Yesterday, Many Opinions Were Expressed on the Examination Regulations

Today's Meeting of the Finance and Equipment Group The Teacher Training Group of the Secondary School Normal School Education Research Conference held its first meeting at 2:00 p.m. yesterday at the YMCA of the Eight Immortals Bridge. Today at 2:00 p.m., the Finance and Equipment Group will be held at the same location. The details are recorded as follows:

Teacher Training Group Members present were Chen Kemei, Cui Jianwu, Sheng Zhensheng, Xu Guangren, Tang Naikang, Yu Guangyao, Feng Yixian, Jia Foru, Qi Zhengcheng, Li Cheng, Shen Yanxiang, etc. Zeng Shengdian and Qian Fugong from the Education Bureau were present. Chairman Chen Kemei studied the following issues: (1) Opinions on the Provisional Regulations for the Examination of Teachers in Secondary Schools and Normal Schools. The discussion results were: (1) For points 1 and 2 of item 1 of Article 4 of the regulations and points 1 and 2 of item 3, graduates of domestic and foreign universities should be treated equally. (2) The word "after" in each item under Article 4 of the regulations should be changed to the word "and". (3) Clause 4 of item 1 of Article 4, Clause 5 of item 2, and Clause 4 of item 3 should be changed to those who have been inspected by the supervisor or certified by the principal as having excellent results. (2) Suggestions on improving the teacher training institutions in secondary schools. The discussion results were: (1) Normal schools should be independent and focus on training above the specialized subject. (2) The number of education colleges in universities should be reduced, and the number of teacher training specialized subjects should be increased. (3) How should teachers in secondary schools and normal schools continue their studies? The discussion results were: (1) The Ministry of Education should be requested to order all provinces and cities to effectively implement the methods decided at the Second National Education Conference. (2) The Ministry of Education should be requested to order all provinces and cities to effectively implement the regulations for secondary schools and normal schools that teachers should take a one-year sabbatical every five years of teaching for further study and be paid their original salary. (3) The methods for improving the operation of summer schools and summer seminars should be (1) paying attention to the discussion of practical problems, and (2) lectures should be reduced.

Finance and Equipment Group The Finance and Equipment Group is scheduled to hold a meeting at 2:00 p.m. today at the YMCA of the Eight Immortals Bridge. The issues for discussion proposed by the Ministry of Education are: (1) How should the equipment for natural sciences in secondary schools and normal schools be improved? (2) Opinions on equipment standards. (3) What percentage of the total school funding should be estimated for teaching equipment expenses? (4) Opinions on the Ministry's order on financial allocation standards. (5) How to reform the forgery of bills and the shortcomings of shops, so that money can be returned to the public. Members Ni Wenya, Yan Zhenyu, Yan Junxuan, Cui Jian, Zhang Shilin, Qi Zhengcheng, Lu Songqian, and Xu Suzhou.

The Central Team is Getting More and More Courageous, Defeated the Nanxing Team Yesterday, the Result was 59 to 30, Central Team vs. Xiexing Today
