In the contest, the Central team was exceptionally brave, especially "Flying Legs" Liu Daguan and giant Tian Kang were the most outstanding, playing vigorously and colorfully. Nanxing was helpless and lost with a score of 30 to 59. Today at 4:00 p.m., the last battle will be fought at Shenyuan with the Xiexing Sports Equipment Company. The competition situation yesterday is briefly described below:

First half After the start of the game, Nanxing took the lead. After Chen Hu opened the record, Zhou Nu'an and Liu Jingfeng scored two goals each, and six points were hung high on the scoreboard. The Central team was unwilling to show weakness, and Tang Shaohua bravely stood up and shot from a distance. Nanxing's Zhou and Chen doubled back, leading 10 to 2. Seeing that the situation was not good, the Central team requested a timeout to secretly plan the strategy. When the battle started again, the Central team really succeeded. Tang Shaohua scored first, Liu Daguan made contributions later, and Tian Kang competed with them, and took the lead with 14 to 10. From then on, the Central team suddenly became powerful. Liu and Tian shot at will, and none of them missed. The score rose like a clear cloud. At the end of the first half, the Central team took the lead with a huge score of 42 to 15.

Second half At the beginning of the second half, Fu Xingzhi tried to reverse the situation, and the Central team also refused to give in, so the situation became more tense. Relying on the strength of Liu Daguan, Tian Kang, etc., the Central team's score increased layer by layer. Although Nanxing tried hard to counterattack, it often lost more than it gained. The largest difference in score was 47 to 15. Later, Liu Jingfeng worked hard and chased it to 53 to 20. At this time, Nanxing's new force Liu Jiang immediately responded and transferred Zhang Daqi, and the military situation was greatly shaken. Liu Jingfeng made two free throws, Chen Hu turned around under the basket, and Zhou Chen met each other from left and right, creating a situation of 53 to 28. The Central team Rongzhao made two penalties and one throw, and Daguan's contribution was not inferior. Nanxing's Chen Hu shot a goal, and the score surged to 59 to 30. The Central team won a great victory.

The results are not only related to national honor, but the participating athletes are also a selection of elite forces. Its importance is self-evident. Long jump final. 11. Javelin throw final. 12. High jump final. 13. Pole vault final. 14. Each unit is allowed to enter three athletes in each event, except for the 220-yard dash and low hurdles, where only two athletes are allowed.

Municipal Elementary School Sports Meet: Meeting of District Preparatory Committee Members. This Year's Exercise Drill Cancelled. Scheduled Dates for District Preparatory Committees Announced

The Municipal Bureau of Education convened a meeting of the preparatory committee members from each district for this year's district elementary school sports meet at the Municipal No. 1 Sports Field on Dajilu yesterday afternoon at 2 PM. Wang Keyong, Zhang Yongchun, and Hu Zongfan from the Bureau of Education, as well as more than forty preparatory committee members from each district, attended. Wang Keyong chaired the meeting, and the proceedings were as follows:

Report Items: First, the chairman reported: (1) The municipal elementary school sports meet has been held at the Municipal No. 1 Sports Field every year. However, due to the increasing number of participants each year, the venue has become too small, causing difficulties, and it is also inconvenient for schools in rural areas to travel back and forth. Therefore, starting this year, a district-based approach will be adopted. (2) In order to promote universal physical education, the Bureau of Education has cancelled individual championships this year. The top five teams in each district will receive team championships. (3) Judges will be appointed on a rotating basis by each district and will consist of physical education teachers from various schools. (4) The chairmen and committee members of each district preparatory committee will be appointed by the Bureau of Education. (5) This year's exercise drill and school song will not be held. (6) The 80-meter low hurdles event will only be held in Districts 1 and 2.

Discussion Items: Decisions: (1) The standing long jump will not use a springboard and will be performed on flat ground without a sandpit. (2) The style of athlete number cloths will be uniformly 4 inches high and 6 inches wide, indicating male/female and Group A/B/C, to be filled in by each district preparatory committee. (3) Students who have graduated from each school but are currently studying at the original school are not allowed to participate. (4) If there are fewer than six athletes participating in each event, the event will not be held. (5) The team exercise and track and field athlete list and the track and field registration form for each school must be submitted to the respective district preparatory committee one week before the meeting date of that district. Late submissions will not be accepted. (6) Schools in Districts 1, 2, and 6 can pick up the various forms at the Municipal No. 1 Sports Field on Dajilu. Schools in other districts should pick them up from their respective district preparatory committees.

Preparatory Committee Dates: The dates for the first meeting of each district preparatory committee have already been decided as follows: District 1: May 3 (Friday) at 2 PM at the Municipal No. 1 Sports Field; District 2: May 2 (Thursday) at 2 PM at Qiu Jiang Elementary School; District 3: April 30 (Tuesday) at 2 PM at Wusong Elementary School; District 4: April 30 (Tuesday) at 2:30 PM at Xinlu Normal School; District 5: April 29 (Monday) at 2 PM at Yangjing Elementary School; District 6: May 1 (Wednesday) at 2 PM at Nanyang Model Elementary School; District 7: April 29 (Monday) at 2 PM at Shicun Elementary School; District 8: April 27 (Saturday) at 2 PM at the Education Association of Jinda District 11.

District Chairmen: The chairmen and committee members of each district preparatory committee have already been appointed by the Bureau of Education as follows: District 1: Wan Zhu Principal Gu Nan; District 2: Qiu Jiang Principal Yan Zhengqing; District 3: Wusong Principal Zhang Shuqin; District 4: Jiazi Principal Cao Huaqiu; District 5: Yangjing Principal Song Jiayu; District 6: Nanyang Model Principal Shen Weiheng; District 7: Shicun Principal Wang Tongde; District 8: Bade Zhenru Principal Wang Deheng.

My Philosophy as a Basketball Referee (3)

— Written by Mr. Dahl of the United States, Translated by Qian Yiqin

The extent to which fouls influence the outcome of a game has been studied and is still being studied. In the "Sports Monthly," the author has written a considerable assessment on this point. This type of research does not include errors by players and coaches, so the responsibility for declaring fouls is placed entirely on the shoulders of the referee, while other factors in the game (such as missed shots by each team) are not included, which is unfair.

If these factors are presented, the situation will be completely different. In a close game, one team lost by three points. Upon checking the game record, it was found that the team missed 49 shots. After the game, while showering, the referee was stopped by the losing team's captain, who blamed him for not calling enough fouls on the opposing defense, which prevented his forwards from attacking and led to the loss. This was the losing team captain's main point of contention. He never considered that his own team missed 49 shots, and these shots were close to the basket. If his own team's shooting was slightly more accurate, even with only a few of these opportunities, the game's record would have been completely different.

Summary of the above opinions: The above opinions are written for novice referees. The following are some more specific opinions that need to be discussed. Before elaborating, the author wants to summarize the opinions that have already been presented:

(1) There is no secret to a referee's success. Hard work accounts for most of the victory and will lead to ultimate success. Furthermore, a referee must have a love and deep passion for refereeing that far exceeds any material reward. There is no one who can achieve true success with the sole purpose of monetary gain. Therefore, one must always maintain a spirit of deep love for this game. Otherwise, the referee is simply a walking corpse. As for poor officiating, monetary rewards cannot comfort the referee's inner pain after the game. Even if it can make them feel comforted by unfair criticism, it is not enough to alleviate the feeling of unease in their throat. If their officiating is poor during the game and their decisions are inappropriate, it will hinder the outcome of the game. Therefore, the first suggestion is: if you want to be a successful referee, you must work hard and continuously.

(2) During the game, one must declare fouls according to the rules. Therefore, one must be very familiar with every rule. There is no need to carry the rules onto the field. In fact, if you can remove a novice referee's hesitation and have confidence, then there is no need to carry the rules around.

(3) Once you are familiar with the rules, you only need to declare fouls according to the rules, without bias or fear.

(4) One must have sharp eyesight and be able to see everything. When a single person is refereeing, they must also take into account the ball and other parts outside of where the players are gathered, especially when jumping the ball, they must look behind them. It is said that one must have eyes in the back of their head.

(5) Sharp eyesight alone is not enough. One must also have quick and immediate judgment and make decisions. After a foul is discovered, it should be announced immediately. Pay extra attention to this aspect, and the difficulty of being a referee will be reduced.

(6) Regardless of who you come into contact with—players, coaches, other staff, and spectators—you must be practical and not meddlesome, courteous but not flattering. One must know the value of self-control, which is no less important than familiarity with the rules, an abundance of common sense, quick judgment, and a brave heart. No matter what situation may arise, no matter who may lose their composure, a referee must not do so. Many spectators may become carried away due to the intensity of the game, but this is their right. In fact, their frenzy during the game comes at a price. It is common for players and coaches to lose their self-control during intense and exciting games. This is only human nature. However, a referee must maintain self-control from beginning to end during intense and exciting games, and remain calm. No matter how serious the mistakes of players or coaches may be, it must still be so. When the words and actions of players or coaches cross the line and are inappropriate, they can naturally be punished by giving the other team a free throw. However, when declaring a technical foul, it must be done with caution and executed with care.

Attitude towards the audience: Do not use technical characteristics to give a team a free throw and make an enemy of the audience. The habit of declaring fouls to the audience often seems unfair to the penalized team, because the audience's behavior is often not related to the seemingly deserved punishment. According to the author's many experiences, it is better to stop the game and explain the reason for declaring the foul. Generally, the good-spirited members of the audience can often stop the bad ones. Sometimes this method cannot be implemented, then it is best to ignore the audience completely. There was one time when the author let a team have as many as eight free throws before the opposing audience calmed down, and although this pass was secure, he was terrified when he thought about what to do if the audience still did not stop. Therefore, other methods are still preferable. Although the last resort is still to declare a foul on the audience. The above six points are the outline of a successful referee. If readers wish to become a referee, they must add common sense and courage, then they have already achieved the beginning of success.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Cold Kiss)

Someone commented on the changing trends of Chinese marriage systems, saying: "The changing trends of Chinese marriage can be roughly divided into (1) mortgage marriage, (2) uxorilocal marriage, (3) remarriage, (4) child betrothal, (5) waiting-for-husband marriage, (6) abduction marriage, (7) adoption marriage, (8) ghost marriage, eight types." They can be described as varied and diverse. It is a pity that no one has tried all eight types, otherwise, if they had tried them all, they would have tasted the sour, sweet, bitter, and spicy flavors of life.

It is said that Zhang Zongchang once taught his son like this: "Look at me, I am all courage. You only know how to study. I don't know a single word, but I also made this great career. There are many unemployed people in China, all because they were educated." Although his words are absurd, upon reflection, they are quite humorous.

Mr. Wu Zhihui recently told someone: "Rescuing the country from its difficulties only requires opening up three major roads, and success can be achieved. The first is to revive the countryside, the second is to complete the bandit suppression plan, and the third is to prepare the latest weapons." If we can do this, then the lost land can be recovered and the national crisis can be resolved naturally.

Han Fuju, the chairman of Shandong Province, governs Shandong extremely strictly. If a smoker is caught, the recidivist is executed by shooting, and the first offender has the character "义" [yi] (righteousness) tattooed on their forehead. It is said that the character "义" is reversed and split apart to mean "I am a tortoise."

Face

— Wei Jing

Actors who perform in operas must wear face paint. Red face paint signifies loyalty, black face paint signifies courage, white face paint signifies treachery, and colorful face paint signifies a clown who makes people laugh—wearing a certain type of face paint represents the identity of a certain type of person.

I think, if all the living beings in this world could express the thoughts in their hearts as clearly as opera actors, then how peaceful would this world be, and how serene would this society be? Naturally, I think, at the very least, there would be no need for mutual deception, because the depths of anyone's mind would be easily understood by others. This perfectly aligns with the saying, "People's hearts are as different as their faces."

However, this is just wishful thinking, just a scene that actors perform on stage. In reality, in this society, there are plenty of people with the faces of robbers but the hearts of bodhisattvas, and there are also plenty of people with the faces of bodhisattvas but the hearts of robbers—although there are also people with the faces and hearts of robbers, or the faces and hearts of bodhisattvas.

Why did God create people with so many different faces? This is truly an eternal enigma that cannot be solved. But I think, if these many different faces could express the status and character of each person like actors do, wouldn't it save a lot of scheming and intrigue in this world? Unfortunately, God did not create people that way.

This truly makes me feel somewhat lost!

Blood

— Hua Ling

Blood is the most precious thing on a person's body. If there is too little blood in a person's body, they will get sick or even die. In ordinary bodies, blood only maintains physiological functions, but the blood in the chests of martyrs is extraordinary—it can awaken the national spirit, wash away national humiliation, restore lost territories, and inspire the cowardly to become brave. But this kind of blood is too precious, and its meaning is too significant, so it can only be found in the bodies of immortal martyrs. In the bodies of ordinary, mediocre people, it is impossible to find even a drop or two, even though it is the same bright red color.

In lower-class society, blood is a synonym for money, as if to say that blood and money are both indispensable to life. But we can often see millionaires suffering from anemia. Although they have so much money, medicine has not yet advanced to the point where colorful banknotes can be injected into the body.

But recently I heard people say that some poor college students in our eastern neighbor, because they don't have money for school, sell their blood to hospitals to be transfused to wealthy people with anemia. In this case, the rich man's money is simply blood, and the poor man's blood is also money, so blood and money are one and the same. Logically speaking, this may not be inconsistent.

If the theory that blood and money are one and the same can be established, then we should love blood and love money. Using foreign goods and letting money flow out is like letting our blood flow out. Keeping this blood can make the country strong. Therefore, here, I wish everyone to cherish all blood and not let it flow away easily.

It is appropriate to use a long-term perspective to see everything.

Correction of Strange Surnames

— Wei Yu

In the previous issue of this publication, there was an article about strange surnames, which mentioned the surname "尢" [wang], claiming that it was pronounced "汪" [wang]. This is a grave error. "尢" is an ancient form of the character "尤" [you]. Any slightly complete dictionary will have a record of this. Those with the surname "尢" actually have the surname "尤" and are absolutely not pronounced "汪". Throughout our country, there are many surnames "尤" without a dot. All surnames "尤" without a dot in Wuxi and Suzhou are descendants of Youfu Jian Gong. Those surnames "尢" in Suzhou, such as those in Liujia Port and Phoenix Street, are all surname "尤" but without a dot. The "尢" in Liujia Port was You Xianjia Dingfu, a leading figure in Suzhou in the past, and he has many descendants. We have never heard of anyone calling him Wang Dingfu. 尢毅, who writes for the Shanghai Xiaoribao, is the alias of You Ban Kuang, and is also not Wang Ban Kuang. Therefore, it is a grave error to claim that the surname "尢" is pronounced "汪".

As for why there is a surname "尤" with and without a dot, and what its origins are, Wei Yu is not clever enough and cannot examine it in detail. Some say that it is because the dot in the character "尤" resembles the character "犬" [quan] (dog), so the dot was removed. This statement seems too absurd, but it can be examined that "尢" is an ancient form of "尤". It is true that the character "尢" is pronounced "汪" when used alone, but the surname "尢" should still be pronounced "尤" and cannot be pronounced "汪", just as the single character 入 [ru] (enter) is pronounced 善 [shan] when used as a surname and not 堆 [dui] (heap). (Additionally, in Liu Xunwei's "Talking About Surnames" on the 12th, Linghu Zhao is a pen name, not the surname Ling, so this is specifically corrected. - Editor's Note)

Random Talk

Old Painter's Family Feast

— Translated by Tao

We often attend the banquets at the old painter Ding Song's house. The night before last, we were invited by lawyer Li Zhishan to spend the whole evening at his place again. Although it was drizzling, everyone's interest was particularly strong. Lawyer Li, despite being a famous legal scholar, has a special connection with the literary and art circles. Most of the people he invited that day were famous figures. When I arrived at the banquet, several distinguished guests had already arrived. The most striking to me was the tall and slender film emperor Jin Yan. What a heroic and cheerful person he was! His alcohol capacity was the most impressive. He liked to drink beer, one cup after another. It was a pity that the petite Ms. Wang Renmei arrived late due to filming. Around ten o'clock, there was a knock on the door. Young Mr. Ding opened the door, and it turned out to be Wildcat jumping in. Jin Yan hurriedly hid his whole body under the round table. Everyone cheered and said: "Old Jin has gone to get drunk." Renmei said: "It doesn't matter if he's gone," but she still didn't believe it and searched around until she found him.

Those who drank sat at one table, and those who didn't drink sat at another. The host was also a generous drinker, so he brought twenty-four drinking games with him. Everyone drew one. The most hilarious one was drawn by Ban Kuang, who had to imitate a dog barking three times. Mr. Shu De, the father of Miss Yuan Meiyun, drew one where he had to imitate a cat meowing three times. Because they refused to meow, they were each fined three cups of wine. Xiong Fei drew one where he had to call Ding's mother "Mom" three times. He called out three times very readily and affectionately. Everyone said: "Young Mr. Ding has another older brother now."

Including Mrs. Ding, there were only four female guests. Miss Yuan Meiyun was of course the focus of everyone's attention. She wore no makeup, and her demeanor was polite and quiet. What artistic talent and great future she has! In addition, singers Yan Fei and Ouyang Feili also enlivened the atmosphere a lot.

Brother Yi Fang and Miss Yan Fei drew lots to sing. Miss Yan was originally a singing saint, and without hesitation, she sang "Su San Don't Cry." Yi Fang, not to be outdone, sang an excerpt from "Cao Cao Captured and Released." Everyone said: "It tastes even better than the [Kirin] School." Some people wanted them to do another one, but they didn't agree. Someone drew a lot where the female guest with permed hair had to drink. It was really strange, none of the four female guests had permed hair. They said: "We are promoting the New Life Movement." Later, it was discovered that Miss Yan's hair had slight curls. Everyone wanted her to sing, but she refused, saying that it was natural and how could she be asked to drink. Someone else drew a lot where the male guest with no hair had to sing. Chen Tingchao's hair was the shortest, and everyone insisted on making him drink. He said: "I have a flat top haircut, how can I drink," but he couldn't resist the public opinion.

When the banquet ended, Jin Yan, Ding Song, Yi Fen, Ban Kuang, and the host Zhishan were still gambling and drinking beer. Mrs. Ding was originally also a heavy drinker, but she drank very little that day because her eyes were a little red. Little-bearded Wu Tianweng hadn't been seen for a long time. He was still wearing a melon-shaped hat with red knots and carrying a walking stick. Ban Kuang said: "Tianweng can be considered to have increased both virtue and age." Mr. Wu said: "Let's leave it to old Mr. Yuan."

These interesting banquets in the literary and art circles have been rare recently, but old painter Ding's house still occasionally has them to add some flavor.

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twelve: Ashamed of Having No Clothes, Hiding Behind Curtains; Working Hard to Save Lamp Oil, Copying Books at Dawn

Zhiqian agreed very much with Zhou Yourong's suggestion, so he beckoned to Wang Beihai. Under the current circumstances, Beihai really had no heart to do extra homework. However, the teacher beckoned for him to go, and he brought his book over. When he arrived at Zhou Yourong's room, the first thing he saw was a high pile of newspapers, large and small. From this, one could tell that he was very concerned about current affairs. He picked up the newspapers on the table with both hands, put them in the corner of the wall, and said with a smile, "Now the table is spacious, you can work." Beihai said: "There is no hurry, we can also go to Mr. Cheng's room to study later." Zhou Yourong said: "I suppose you can't concentrate on reading and listening to lectures here with me. Actually, times are different now. It is impossible to find secluded valleys in deep mountains to study like the ancients. First, the books we read now are based on science. Not only do we need the teacher to explain, but we also need instruments to do experiments. Second, studying to become an official is not what we do now. Now we need to learn skills to make a living in society. When people enter society, they need to be in contact with people everywhere, and modern society is very complicated. In a company's office, there are often dozens of people working in one place. If you practice not being disturbed when writing lists and drafts, it would be useful for the time when you can't get started at all. So, I don't agree with the ancient method of studying behind curtains." Zhiqian said: "What you said is very correct, but Beihai is not afraid that you will disturb him, but he is afraid that he will disturb you." Zhou Yourong said: "I most admire hardworking young people, and I am not afraid of people disturbing me while reading." (191)

Records of Drifting Fragrance

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

What happened after that? It was just taking apart the ornaments on this hat and nailing them onto those phoenix shoes, using them interchangeably; otherwise, it would definitely not be enough. Fortunately, pearls are very durable. Unless you scratch them with something, they will not break easily. So, when a pair of phoenix shoes became too old (definitely not because they were worn too much, let alone being worn out) and no longer needed to be kept, the shoe body would be discarded, but all the pearls would be taken off and handed over to the shoemakers to tidy up for use in decorating new shoes.

There were also two ways to nail pearls onto the shoe surface: the first was the one I mentioned above, first stringing the pearls together with silk threads, and then nailing the silk threads onto the shoe surface; the second was to directly nail the pearls onto the shoe surface one by one, using pearls instead of colored threads to form various patterns. This kind of nailing is not only more solid, but also more refined and elegant than embroidering flowers and then nailing pearls. I remember when I first entered the palace, I praised these phoenix shoes decorated entirely with pearls without restraint. Furthermore, because I was not yet familiar with the Empress Dowager's temper, I openly revealed my admiration. The Empress Dowager's temperament was such that she liked to give people what they admired most, so she immediately ordered people to pick out two pairs of phoenix shoes decorated with pearls in the same way and give them to me. I was naturally very happy to accept them. But from then on, when I saw her new shoes, I dared not praise or admire them like that again, otherwise, she might have given me all the phoenix shoes in the shoe store without any hesitation! But although I didn't get that many, the total number of pairs of phoenix shoes that the Empress Dowager gave me before and after was indeed several dozens. I still treasure three or four pairs to this day! (301)

Miscellaneous: South Korea Prohibits the Import of Armored Scale Insect Plants -- Originally Transmitted to the United States from China

Yesterday, the local Commodity Inspection Bureau received an order from the Ministry of Industry, stating that the Minister of Agriculture of Yugoslavia has ordered a ban on the import of plants infected with pear wheel scale insect Aspidiotus Perniciosus Comst. This pest is widely distributed, and it was first introduced into California, USA, from China, severely impacting the pear industry. Now, it is also found in Chile, Germany, Australia, Japan, Canada, Hawaii, and the South Pacific Islands. It harms over 500 species of plants, including pears, plums, apples, currants, quinces, apricots, cherries, nectarines, rose family plants, mulberry family plants, ground plants, forest shade trees, and ornamental plants, all of which are susceptible to its infestation. If local merchants have plants to be shipped to South Korea, they must be inspected and certified by the Commodity Inspection Bureau before they can be shipped.

Free Talk

Vignettes and Personality

— Qin Wen

In general novels and plays, the so-called "expression of personality" has two meanings. One is the expression of the "character's" personality, which is to write the character's demeanor and temperament in the "story" thoroughly, so that the laborer looks like a laborer, the farmer is indeed like a farmer, the young person has the characteristics of a young person, and the old person has the appearance of an old person; moreover, what kind of work the young person is engaged in, how old the laborer is, whether it is a man or a woman, are all described in detail and naturally. The character's beliefs and thoughts are also directly and indirectly revealed at a glance. The second is the expression of the author's own personality; in addition to ideology, it also has relationships with "local color," "era," and "nationality," etc.

Only when the author's own personality is expressed can it be considered a mature work. The personality of a great writer is strong, and it is revealed richly and invisibly; therefore, even if their works are not signed, readers who are accustomed to their other works can recognize them. However, in general novels and plays, the so-called expression of personality is more focused on the first meaning, especially in the new literature; because the purpose is to explore problems, as long as it is written carefully, is rich in "realism," and can arouse the reader's "resonance" and have a positive impact, its value already exists. Moreover, the expression of the character's personality can be deliberately worked on; the author's own personality must be revealed unintentionally, coming from nature, which is desirable but not achievable.

Vignettes do not need to have a fixed "structure," do not need to abide by the "unities," and may as well write according to the author's subjective feelings, changing as the situation changes; of course, the personality of the characters cannot be meticulously described in detail. Moreover, the length is small; short stories will not emphasize the detailed expression of the character's personality like long novels and plays, but rather focus on brevity; moreover, vignettes need to address many points.

According to what has been said above, in vignettes, the character's personality is difficult to express, at least not fluently. So, what about the author's own personality? This is important; it does not need to have a fixed structure, and does not need to abide by the unities, so it seems easy to do. Although it is easy to do, it is difficult to write something wonderful and outstanding. The problem lies precisely in its freedom; everyone can do it casually, and it is difficult to attract attention without uniqueness. Therefore, vignettes must express the author's own personality, which means that it is easy to move people only when there is considerable maturity. General novels and plays, or can use intellectual "techniques" to make them outstanding; but moving vignettes must have a considerable natural expression of emotion.

Some may think that emotion is blind, and that the exploration of life's problems through naturally expressed emotion may lack meaning, or even be wrong. But this is not the case. As long as the ideology held is great and the thought is correct, even if it is revealed unintentionally, it will not be wrong. Originally, a person rich in an idea is also rich in the emotion of this idea; for example, a person rich in revolutionary thought is also rich in revolutionary emotion. A person who holds an ideology is always biased in thought, that is, has a "preconceived notion," and always observes things as if wearing colored glasses. Therefore, for the same horse, a painter always focuses on color and shape, military officers and doctors probably focus on fat and thinness and strength, while biologists focus on the structure and temperament of the limbs.

Because it is a natural expression, without pretense and hypocrisy, it is the true face of the author. Therefore, although vignettes are short, they occupy an important position in the basic principle of literature, "the expression of personality."

Daqing Mountain

— Yuan Chenying

Our group of more than sixty people, divided among four large automobiles, headed towards the Mongolian plains. Leaving the outskirts of Guihua, we entered the long mountain gully in front of the towering Daqing Mountain (Note 1) beyond the border. The water had already dried up, and the large and small green stones jolted us in the cars as we drove over them.

Walking ahead of us were pedestrians wearing tattered and dirty short clothes, each carrying a small bundle on their backs and shoulders - containing all their belongings. For the sake of livelihood, they left their warm homes to cultivate land in the wilderness, plant crops, and do small businesses, only to return home at the end of the year with the few coins they earned to live some happy days. They have a saying, "walking the back mountain (Note 2)." These people are those who walk the back mountain.

The cars drove into the mountain pass, but the two cars behind us suddenly disappeared from sight.

There are not many trees on the mountain. The grass is still withered and yellow, and only a few small willow trees sway in the wind on the hillside; the telegraph poles from Guihua to Wuchuan stand tall on the mountaintops and slopes. Besides the "back mountain walkers" and the occasional ox carts coming from the opposite direction, no sound could be heard in the mountains: only the loud singing of our companions added some liveliness to the silent valley.

After crossing the rocky gully, we arrived at the dam opening, but the two cars behind us still hadn't arrived. After waiting for an hour, several people went down to the hillside at the entrance to look, but they couldn't see a trace of them. One of the cars traveling with us drove away first: so we decided not to wait any longer.

After leaving the village at the dam opening, we hadn't gone far when we saw the car that was waiting for us. Several girls jumped out of the car and sat under a withered tree, worried: "Should we go or not?" Everyone asked. "Let's go, let's go! Let's go to Wuchuan to wait for them!" Finally, we decided on this plan.

Before we had gone two miles, the car had to climb a very steep hillside. At the entrance to the hillside, there were several walls made of rough stones and a few small earthen houses. Several families had white words written on them saying "lodging available." The elderly and some women with bound feet, as well as children, looked at us with surprise, whispering, "Look! Where did so many foreign students come from? Huh! There are even female students who don't wear buns!"

The car roared several times, and some of the "back mountain walkers" ahead climbed up the small path on the hillside and left. The car climbed up the hillside, leaning backwards as if it were about to tip us over. The car moved so slowly, and at a bend in the mountain corner, the girls' car climbed up first. Dirt flew up, rushing into everyone's noses. They waved their handkerchiefs to signal to the people in our car. At this time, I looked down, and my heart couldn't help but beat rapidly. We were almost to the top of the mountain now, and the city of Guihua in front of us was just a dark mass. Thick snow was still piled up in the shady areas of the mountain, and the weather was a bit colder than before.

The car climbed to the highest mountaintop, where the "Obo" (Note 3) stood, and then it was downhill. Here, we could no longer see the city, only the snow on the mountaintops and the white clouds reflecting each other.

Going downhill was a little easier. The car slowly drove down like a snail. We had to be very careful at the turns, otherwise there would be a danger of flipping from the mountain into the ditch.

On the last hillside, a mountain god temple stood there, truly having the aura of "one man guarding the pass, ten thousand men cannot enter." At the junction of the hillside and the ditch, there were four large characters carved on the rock by Ji Hongwei in the fourteenth year of the Republic of China: "Turning Danger into Safety." Only here did we truly relax.

After going down the hillside, we entered the mountain gully again, but this time there was water flowing gurglingly. The ice had not completely melted, and snow was piled high on the ice. When the mountain wind blew, it actually blew up thin ice like pieces of paper, like small butterflies flying.

By the time we left the mountain gully, it was almost dusk. The color of the land also changed, with red, black, and yellow soil. The low city walls of Wuchuan County appeared before our eyes. Because we were waiting for those two cars, we stayed here for the night.

Note 1, "Daqing Mountain" is the Yinshan Mountains. Note 2, "Walking the back mountain" means people who go to the Mongolian plains behind Daqing Mountain and the villages in Wuchuan County to make a living. Note 3, "Obo" is a Mongolian word, translated into Chinese as a pile of soil, used by Mongolians as a marker.

Little Beggar

— Qi Xuan

Still unable to use fate to explain himself,

His mind hasn't turned to this yet.

Understandingly looking at his father's dry, withered lips,

He learned three or five bitter words of a beggar.

Withered yellow face, scorched black hands,

Heaven knows he hasn't touched water in a hundred days;

His face has never seen a smile nor thought of crying,

From birth, he has been in this hazy state.

When other people's beautiful children pass by him,

It doesn't stir up even a slight wave in his mind,

His eyes don't even dare to look up and see,

He's afraid of the dog-beating stick in the adult's hand.

His small stomach is empty and keeps calling out,

The soreness on his kneecaps keeps increasing;

Kneeling all day, he can't even get a few coppers,

In reality, this small life can't last many years.

Mountain Pastoral (5)

— Ai Wu

The man took the dry tobacco, put it in his mouth, and began to suck hard without using the mouthpiece. His eyes glanced at Boss Qin, who was standing there wanting to come over but not daring to, and said to Lao Chen:

"Is he one of your group?"

"No, just traveling on the same road!" After Lao Chen replied, he shouted loudly: "Hey, Boss Qin, come over and take a rest!"

And he called out the three words "Boss Qin" especially loudly, as if deliberately trying to make people notice.

Boss Qin slowly walked over, revealing a look of surprise and unease.

The man saw that Boss Qin was limping as he walked, and only after he had come close did he ask:

"Hey, has this friend of yours not walked a long road before?"

"Heh, sir, how can he be like us selling our strength: grinding our bones and nourishing our intestines. He's a big boss doing foreign goods business, can't you tell?"

At this point, even Lao Chen pretended to be a coolie. Boss Qin, hearing that he was being flattered under such circumstances, was like an apprentice who had been slapped by his master, and quickly put on a look of complaining and protested:

"Me, how can I look like a boss? My mouth and eyes don't match up at all! I'm just helping people with their accounts. Speaking of it, I'm also helping others, doing whatever they tell me to do. How can I compare to you doing small business? With your own capital, no one dares to interfere! How dare us abacus bead counters even hum a breath in front of the big bosses?"

Boss Qin's eloquence was not weaker than others, and in addition to defending himself, he also tried his best to expose Lao Chen's pretense of being a coolie.

The man seemed to dislike hearing these words and took the tobacco branch off to ask Lao Xu:

"Hey, do you have any pastries for sale?"

Lao Xu blushed and answered awkwardly, while unconsciously scratching his ear.

"No, I just carry some odds and ends, not worth even a copper, even if I dropped them on the side of the road, I'm afraid no one would even look at them!"

The man flicked off a bit of ash from the tobacco branch, repeated placing it in his mouth, and took a big puff, closing his eyes tightly, as if the deliciousness of the tobacco had made him completely forget that there were other people in front of him.

Lao Chen had been glaring hatefully at Boss Qin, but at this moment he turned his gaze and looked at the man's face, asking worriedly:

"May I ask what kind of business you are in, sir?"

The man opened his eyes and asked back with a smile:

"Take a look, what kind of business am I in?"

"Hmm!..."

Lao Chen blushed and couldn't answer.

Crossing the Huai River

— Shen Shengshi

The wheels rolled over the uneven stone-paved small streets, making me feel sick in my stomach from the bumps in the car.

When we arrived at the wharf, I breathed a sigh of relief, got out of the car, and walked down to the small steamer with Mr. Ji. Looking inside and outside the cabin, the deck, and the stern, it was all full of passengers. I asked the boatman to find us a place to stand, and after thinking for a moment, perhaps because we were wearing long robes, he almost treated us very favorably, leading us to a small room that was the accounting clerk's living quarters on the boat. The volume could seat four or five people, and now it was comfortable enough for the two of us to sit inside.

It was already nine o'clock, but the boat kept whistling and didn't leave.

There must be a reason for not leaving!

Suddenly, a boatman poked his head in through the window and said to us: - Please sit outside!

- Strange, you asked us to come in! Is there a free place outside? Why are you saying this?

- We are not leaving because we are waiting for an official, and this room is to be given to the official to sit in.

This really made us angry.

- No way, you can invite the official to sit with us, we won't leave. I said to him.

Because the official hadn't arrived yet, the boatman went away with a lingering face. After a while, he poked his head in through the window again, with an almost pleading expression.

- Please... please sit outside! The official is coming soon.

- You invite the official in, we can all sit together, there are enough seats!

- No, the official has guards, the official should sit alone.

- Nonsense, where is there a regulation that this small room on your boat should only be for officials to sit in.

We finally didn't leave. I thought to myself, I really don't know what kind of remarkable official this is, an official riding a boat, kicking out the common people, being an official always has prestige; but we two are too detestable, not afraid of officials, this is really a bit unimaginable.

The sailing time had been delayed by an hour, but the boat still didn't leave, because the official hadn't arrived yet; the common people on the boat had no choice but to wait bitterly.

Finally, the official arrived after delaying the sailing time by an hour and a half, bringing a small guard who looked like a child, and came to our small room.

It turned out that the so-called official was a company commander of a certain army, wearing a gray old military uniform, with a weathered face, yellow and thin; as if I had known there would be a bad omen, I hurried to let him sit down, but before he sat down, he hummed in his throat, and spat two mouthfuls of thick phlegm onto the deck, almost sticking to the back of my shoes.

He ordered his guard to push our luggage aside, and then lay down to sleep without caring about anything. The boat hadn't even traveled half a mile, and the company commander was already snoring loudly.

At this time, Mr. Ji and I were a little annoyed. Had we known that such an official was going to come in, we should have let him sit alone, and it would have been more refreshing to stand on the bow and watch the waves!

Dancing Marathon (5)

— (By American J.T. Farrell) Translated by Yi Xian

His dancing was exhausted, and she wrapped her arms around his neck or hips, and rested her head on him, falling asleep. He wearily dragged her around the floor, and when he fell asleep, she did the same to him. Several times, their bodies collided with each other, rocking, pushing, and then he developed a desire for her, and felt her closeness gradually become depressing. Especially when the night was very deep, and the audience in the dance hall was sparse, he noticed deeply that she would often rub her body against him, look hotly into his eyes, and tell him some lewd jokes. Other dancers also became like this. Several told him that he was being made soft all over by some girl.

Day after day, the "Marathon" continued. His eyes were heavy. His back ached. His feet were sore and stiff, and every step he took was painful. He often felt as if he were treading on fire. The dance hall was filled with the persistent mist of cigarette smoke, and permeated with the turbid odor of human bodies. He felt almost entirely dirty, sweaty, and itchy. Dust fluttered into his nostrils and eyes. He had a fit of coughing. His veins stood out. He became a person who was always half-awake, and everything was almost like a dream. Mary also changed. Her hips swelled up. Dark circles formed deeply beside her eyes, and she looked haggard, her face red and swollen, looking like an extremely exhausted prostitute. She energetically dabbed on grease and powder, and her face became a ghostly image of a cartoon-like dancer.

In the beginning, mostly because of his accent and Greek demeanor, Taxis was the subject of many jokes. Several times, people asked him why he didn't work as a waiter in a restaurant, serving customers a plate of beef buns. He got the nicknames "waiter," "water shop waiter," "Socrates," and "beef buns." Gradually, these nicknames had been called for so long that they no longer aroused his anger. Dancing plunged his body and mind into habitual sorrow and pain. He and all the other contestants always longed to breathe some fresh air. During their breaks, if they weren't too tired to move, they would drag themselves like sleepwalkers to the small beds to lean against for a while, or else go into the narrow dressing rooms or unclean toilets, stick their heads out of the windows to breathe some fresh air, and look down at the tireless people walking freely on the streets.

Day after day passed. Sometimes Taxis, Mary, or other contestants went through six hours, twelve hours, a whole day, or even longer, in a daze. After this time, they turned to a crude, struggling state of excitement, and after this state of excitement, they fell into a daze again. Especially when it was very late at night, if they were awake, they often became crude, struggling, and cursing. Sexual desire also became a gradually expanding magic power, sometimes simply going crazy. Being so close to each other, their bodies touching each other so often, they teased each other even more lewdly. Suffering and desire burned fiercely within them. This became a series of tragic mental and physical pains. Like constipation, diarrhea, and sudden dysfunctions of the kidneys and bladder, there was always a contestant walking around the floor or being dragged around sleepily, with wet lines flowing down their pants or the large bloomers that the dancers were used to wearing. Also, bleeding, bruises on the feet. Also headaches, eye diseases, sore throats, fever and chills. Waves of sweating, followed by shivering, chills. This often led back to unconsciousness, the cause of unconsciousness being insomnia and fatigue, various dreams and fantasies, which they used as a process to relieve suffering while they circled on the floor. The end of this process was money, the chance to become famous, sexual desire, clean white sheets, and soft and comfortable beds.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

Impoverished China

— Meng Ruo

China, which has always prided itself on its vast territory, abundant resources, and large population, is now a bankrupt and dilapidated household. Exactly how much wealth this bankrupt and dilapidated household of ours has has never been accurately surveyed, so it is not very clear. However, according to Japanese statistics, the comparison of the wealth of our country with that of the great powers is as follows:

Country Total National Wealth (Japanese Yen) Average Wealth per Person (Japanese Yen)

United States 762,256,000,000 6,607

United Kingdom 236,320,000,000 5,247

France 103,530,000,000 2,549

Japan 102,343,000,000 1,731

Germany 71,850,000,000 1,441

Italy 44,786,000,000 1,117

China 38,289,000,000 101

What method the Japanese used for this statistics has not been investigated? Whether the figures in the statistical table are reliable is also unknown. If the Japanese statistics are accurate and reliable, then from this statistical table, we can see that the poverty of the Chinese people is truly extreme. The difference in the degree of wealth between our country and the great powers is truly astonishing. In terms of total national wealth, our country is about 20 times less than the United States, and even compared to Japan, it is nearly three times less. In terms of average wealth per person, our country is more than 60 times less than the United States, and even compared to Japan, it is more than ten times less. Of course, the United States is the richest country in the world, how can we compare to them? But we are not only not as good as the United States, even Japan is far ahead of us. Moreover, among these seven countries, our country is the poorest. This cannot but alarm people and cause endless worries about the country's economic future.

There are probably two reasons for China's poverty. One reason is the economic invasion of the great powers. After the Opium War, the country's important gateways were blasted open by foreign cannons. Following the cannons, there was a constant influx of goods from various countries. As a result, China had a huge trade deficit, with hundreds of millions of dollars flowing out every year. This has gradually depleted China's wealth. Another reason is that resources have not yet been developed. China has abundant resources all over the country. However, due to transportation, capital, technology, and other factors, these resources have not yet been developed for human use. This is also the reason why China has not been able to become rich and strong.

For the present plan, to alleviate China's economic difficulties, on the one hand, we should start by revitalizing industry and resisting foreign economic aggression. On the other hand, we must find ways to develop resources as soon as possible. Recently, following the New Life Movement, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has also promoted a National Economic Construction Movement. The purpose of this movement is to enable China's national economy and people's livelihood to reach a stable state. If this movement is widely implemented, it will surely benefit China's economic future.

Night on the Qiantang River

— Luo Jia

The river surface is rendered exceptionally beautiful by the lingering glow of the setting sun, even as those purple small boats with their white sails drift away into the distance! But the emerald peaks and verdant trees along the opposite riverbank, the charming ancient temple pagoda silhouettes, and the gentle smiles of the boat girls facing the tender river breeze, bestow upon this twilight river an endless charm.

However, the setting sun has, after all, set! On the twilight river, only a vast expanse of twilight mist prevails: softly rising up is the singing of little songs by the young lads rowing their boats!

"Set sail!" The owner of our awninged boat shouted at the top of his lungs at the bow of the boat, so that the passengers could get on board sooner. In fact, the cabin was already packed with people, so the boat immediately left the riverbank.

The boat glided forward smoothly and effortlessly on the river, propelled by the late spring breeze. The voyage on this small boat, calculated in time, is only one night. But calculated in distance, it is about thirty miles! When the passengers, having slept overnight on the boat's wooden planks, were awakened by the sounds of oars and paddles, the sun had just half risen above the river surface, and our awninged boat had already safely reached its destination.

In the late spring season, the daytime is often a little sultry; once night falls, especially on the river, even though one is wearing a lined shirt, one feels cool and light. The cabin was crammed with fourteen people, so it was very noisy, but when the bright moon shone directly upon the river's heart, and the silver light spilled onto the faces of the passengers in the cabin, they would rub their weary eyes and say:

"It's late at night!"

And so they would lie down one by one, and before long, they were all joyfully enjoying the pleasure of sleep! But me! I often suffer from insomnia, even when not traveling: thus I quietly murmured to myself:

"Travelers without travel worries are fortunate."

Leaning on the gunwale, listening to the splashing of water beneath the boat, it was very crisp and clear: if my sentiments were more refined, perhaps I would "beat the side of the boat and sing," but alas, I am as dull as a deer or pig, and can only gaze at the moonlit scenery of the Qiantang River!

A patch of azure sky, in the very center of which is set a round moon, perhaps it is too lonely, without a single cloud to accompany it. The river surface evenly rises with tiny waves, forever at an even pace. The surroundings are extremely quiet, sometimes one or two white-feathered waterfowl flap their wings, brushing past the boat awning, leaving behind a sorrowful long cry, trembling the fragile hearts of travelers. The moon sent our boat past Heron Shoal. There, the midnight crowing of village roosters had already been heard, sound by sound; in the village, it seemed someone was carrying a lantern walking at night, and at this time, halfway up the mountain, there also seemed to be two or three points of light, these were probably will-o'-the-wisps!

The cabin brushed past a clump of reeds, and a flock of wild ducks lodging in the reeds all flew up, scattering in a panic. Among them, one, perhaps sleepy-eyed, broke into the cabin, but it immediately realized this was not its place of return, and flew away; but it had strayed too far from the flock!

The night chill pierced the bones, the dew dampened my lined shirt, I believed that tomorrow's morning was near, and so I prepared to pass the remaining small journey in a dream, arriving safely at my home.

A Son Without Parents

— Ruizhi

"Savage," was a little playmate of mine when I was a child, and also the son of Battalion Commander Li, who lived next door.

His character was very rough, from childhood he was extremely mischievous, among our group of children, although his age was considered the smallest, he became the leader of our group. He had great strength, was most adept at fighting, so whenever there were fights or wrestling matches with others, he was always at the forefront. He often beat other children, and would not stop until the person being beaten cried. After beating people, he would grin ferociously, and even when facing people he couldn't defeat, he wouldn't yield. Therefore, the children in the vicinity were all afraid of him, and everyone gave him the nickname "Savage." Gradually, even the adults called him "Savage," and his original name was almost forgotten by everyone.

His father was a soldier, and that kind of fierce behavior and character could be seen in his treatment of his son and wife. He would often beat his son or wife so that everyone nearby knew, because of some small matter or because he had drunk a little too much wine. His father's character was completely passed on to "Savage," and was even more severe than his father's.

His mother committed suicide after giving birth to him. His current mother is a prostitute whom his father remarried, because his father was a soldier and was not at home many days of the year, his young mother, who was a prostitute by origin, although she was already around thirty years old, but because she was used to that life of dazzling lights and fine wines, so everyone nearby knew that she was keeping a lover. "Savage" also knew a little about this, so the mother of that lover didn't care much about disciplining him. Because of this, this inherently mischievous child was even more dissolute, making him fully a wild child without any education.

We children called him "Savage" because he was a somewhat uncivilized person, but the adults called him by this nickname for other reasons. I often heard people ask him:

"How did your mother die? Who is raising you?"

When people asked him this, he would be stunned and not know how to answer, he could only loudly answer people:

"Dead is dead, ask my father! Damn it."

His sentences always had to include cursing, especially when asked questions he couldn't answer, he would curse people's parents and ancestors.

The women in the neighborhood also disliked him, and would often be heard cursing him as a savage, a bastard without a father, and other curses.

Although people cursed him like that, he himself didn't understand why. We children also didn't understand why.

Later, I gradually learned that his mother used to be the wife of a villager, and because she was beautiful, she was snatched away by his father. His mother's former husband was also killed by his father. He was not born by his father, but when his mother was snatched away, he was already hidden in her belly.

"Savage" himself didn't know any of this. He always thought his father was his biological father. Although he was very savage, he was still a little afraid when he saw his father.

When he was fifteen or sixteen years old, he was considered to have passed the entrance exam to study at a middle school. He gradually had a sense of being human, but unfortunately he learned about his own background, and knew it more clearly than others. After only studying for two years in middle school, he suddenly disappeared. His father searched everywhere, but still didn't know where he had gone. In a letter to his father, he wrote: "...I am an orphan, my parents were both killed by you, if you hadn't raised me for these ten years, I would have killed you to comfort my biological parents..."

Boatmen of the Han River

— Ming Meng

The boatmen of the Han River carry charcoal and firewood, etc., drifting down from the upper reaches of the Han River, far away. Passing through dangerous shoals, rushing through rapid currents, they live under the weight of strong shoulders and arms, until the shoulder pads are scorched black, and long wooden paddles supported on their shoulders form calluses. Only when they reach Xiangzi Bridge can they take a breath. Then they load another kind of cargo from Shantou, and go against the current again, climbing dangerous shoals, rushing through rapid currents, heading straight into the area surrounded by mountains. Life is truly a heavy burden!

Whenever the water rises, the floodwaters at the Xiangzi Bridge stir up huge whirlpools, and the bridge pillars are submerged by the waves. A moment of carelessness, and the boatmen can be smashed to pieces. When the water falls, certain sections of the river will expose the red sand at the bottom, and the heavy weight of the cargo will strand the boat on the accumulated sand. If no one comes to help, using manpower to step into the water and push the boat's hull, the boat simply refuses to move forward. Proceeding through the waterway squeezed between two mountains, a moment of carelessness, and the wooden boat can be shattered by the beach rocks.

However, our Han River boatmen have strong physiques, arms full of strength, and a fighting spirit that fills their whole bodies. They fight with the energy of their lives against nature, struggling with the current, allowing life to continue to exist between this heaven and earth, leaving behind the great achievements of humanity on the vast flow of the Han River.

Our Han River boatmen are also optimistic and accept their fate: lighting a fire on the boat to cook, and having eaten their fill, the great power of life naturally flows out: when working, they hum mountain songs, forgetting their pain. The floodwaters of the Han River are often filled with songs, and the tides at the mouth of the Han River respond to the calls of humanity.

Whenever there is a moonlit night, they step on their own shadows on the embankment of the Han River. Watching the pale white moonlight shining on the floodwaters. The boatmen of the great river flash weak lights, and the boatmen agitate their songs in the air, spreading them to both banks. If they are catching up with the flow of water, the boatmen will still pole at night, unleashing their full energy, sweating all over their bodies,

Page 19

, casting black shadows on the rippling water. The beauty of nature is unrelated to our boatmen, life separates this class from humanity.

Some park their boats by the shore, and buy a few taels of inferior sorghum mixed with spirits from a hotel near a customs post, barely getting drunk in the turbid current, to forget the pain of the day. Whether this situation is painful or happy, our boatmen themselves probably cannot explain.

Bamboo rafts or logs also float on the floodwaters of the Han River. On a row of rafts, temporary dwellings are built. When the water rises, the rafts naturally rush down like flowing arrows, and that situation is naturally easier to navigate than a heavy wooden boat. But in preventing bridge pillars and dangerous shoals, long rafts are difficult to turn around quickly. Even more pitiful is that if one encounters the water drying up, that navigation will be exceptionally difficult.

The boats of the Han River boatmen have a special shape, gradually sharpening the bow and raising it up like the dragon boats in the Dragon Boat Race. To a first-time observer, it seems very interesting, but when our boatmen climb dangerous shoals, this shape can only give them one convenience, to avoid rushing water entering the boat, otherwise they will not feel any interest at all.

Spending a lifetime on the water, grinding their muscles to eat. Now European civilization, however, carries a huge machine power into the interior, and steamboats also come to rampage in the river. Our boatmen already feel the threat to their livelihood, and thinking that one day material civilization will become more developed, where will our boatmen find a place to eat?

Pitiful boatmen of the great river! The fate of Chinese boatmen!

Sino-Foreign Job Agency

— Tianzhen

"No job, stomach rumbling; friends lending money, hard to speak; what to do? - No way out!"

That was a young lad, neither tall nor short, wrinkling his brow, singing softly like this. His feet paced back and forth, as if he had something big on his mind, the room was small, many people were looking at him, laughing at him, like a madman. Even though foreigners were shushing him, he acted as if he didn't hear!

"Are there foreigners too? - Aren't foreigners all rich?" Miss You asked, because the foreigners she saw in the countryside were all full of vigor and seemed rich.

(Aunt Liu moved her chair closer to Miss You, like a mother scolding her daughter.)

This is the Sino-Foreign Job Agency! Aren't there any poor foreigners? There are countless Russian bums: old women, old men. There are also many Chinese people!

"If there weren't so many foreigners, it would be easier for us to find work." Miss You, who had just arrived, saw Shanghai with gold shining all over the place, but after Aunt Liu said this, her heart was poured with cold water, and she turned to resent the unemployed foreigners.

Easier? Not necessarily. First, you have to understand foreign languages, second, you have to be young and beautiful, then they want you. Also, doing things for foreign families is very troublesome! Really.

In the countryside, Aunt Liu lived next door to Miss You, so Miss You naturally trusted her words, and she was an "old Shanghai hand," relying entirely on her instructions: "I heard some can speak Chinese, - don't you speak foreign languages?"

Understanding is naturally good! Like me, if I don't understand clearly, I get scolded, and I lose my job, - you don't know, last year, I changed three employers. Foreigners are really troublesome, they use too much money, or else, they say you stole it, but the clothes have to be changed every two days: for the side dishes, when it's our turn, there's only cold soup and bones to gnaw on, if you leave a little dish in advance, and he sees it, he'll make a big fuss; especially when a guest comes, he's always uneasy, afraid of eating his food, and every time a guest comes, you have to endure a scolding. I advise you, it's better to work for Chinese families.

"I heard foreign families are willing to pay." Miss You's original intention was that because foreigners have a lot of money, that's why she ran out of the countryside; in fact, the original vegetable growing life was barely enough to keep her warm and fed. But you have to be young and beautiful, what to do, she didn't quite understand: "What do you need to be beautiful for? If you can do things, not being deaf or mute is enough."

Beautiful, you just have to be beautiful, foreigners are no good, damn it!

I don't know if it was the heat of the sun shining in from the window, or Aunt Liu felt a little ashamed, but on the face of Aunt Liu, who was almost forty years old, a blush of youth suddenly appeared, she moved the chair away from Miss You a little, Miss You kept looking at her and thought for a while, as if she understood something: "Isn't there a wife? If they're not well-behaved, why don't you tell the wife?"

Tell the wife? You don't understand what they're saying, the result is just that you suffer, either you're scolded and beaten, or you lose your job! The reason for changing three employers last year, half was not understanding the language, half was...

"Are you still beaten? Then how long have you worked here?"

Six months. ...Not beaten? You're not allowed to cry even if you're beaten.

Miss You knew everything about how she could last six months here. Thinking about having to be beautiful, Miss You saw a few black moles on her face in the reflection on the window glass, which seemed to have spread? Looking at the older Aunt Liu, her hair was shiny, and her clothes were very neat, much more beautiful than herself. So she was even more disappointed.

(Silence locked the kitchen, the water on the stove bubbled and called. Aunt Liu got up and opened the kettle lid)

(The stairs creaked, and after a while, a foreign man walked out disconsolately, looking at Aunt Liu with a grin, and when he discovered Miss You sitting in the corner, he put on a stern face.)

"Who is she? What is she doing here! ...Get out!"

Miss You saw that Aunt Liu was just cowering, unable to say anything, she quickly winked at Aunt Liu and walked out the back door. The door slammed shut, and the sound of giggling immediately rose in the room.
