Shenbao Local Supplement Film Special

Every Star Has a Counterpart of the Opposite Sex

— Wen Ying

This is Hollywood's latest discovery: every star, of either sex, must have an equal counterpart of the opposite sex.

These counterparts, male and female stars, are not only similar in appearance and age, but also identical in their professional and personal lives. Their early environments, past histories, and even their temperaments, romances, and number of marriages are all the same. Isn't this Hollywood's most astonishing new discovery?

Hollywood has a male Clark Gable and must also have a female Clark Gable; it has a female Katharine Hepburn and must also have a male Katharine Hepburn. It is said that every movie star in Hollywood has an equal counterpart of the opposite sex. Even Greta Garbo, who is considered unique, has a male counterpart. The journalist who made this discovery specifically selected eight female stars and eight male stars, matching them up in pairs to prove his strange finding.

The first pair he mentioned was Clark Gable and the Russian actress Anna Sten. If you place their facial profiles side by side, you can see that, apart from Clark Gable's characteristic hair, eyebrows, and mustache, the rest of their eyes, noses, mouths, etc., are all similar. Not only do they look alike, but their early experiences were also largely the same. One in a village in Ohio, the other in a small town in Russia, both suffered hardships in their childhoods. They both started learning acting at the same time. They both married someone who greatly benefited their future but with whom they could not live happily. One married a great Russian actor, and the other married a famous drama instructor. They both divorced in 1928 in two different places.

Later, they both married people older than themselves. They both became famous for their strong and unyielding style. Their temperaments are also the same. They both love the outdoors and being close to nature. They both have healthy physiques. They both like the ordinary and have no exoticism. Finally, their skin tones and the sound of their voices are very similar.

Greta Garbo and Ronald Colman are a pair of cynical actors on the screen. If you put their photos side by side, you can see that they have a surprising resemblance. They both reveal a deep worldly experience. Of course, their experiences came from equally unhappy love affairs. One due to the breakup of her love with Mauritz Stiller, and the other due to the failure of his marriage in England. They both have an unapproachable attitude. Recently, they each purchased property, preparing for retirement. Strangely, nineteen months ago, they left Hollywood at the same time and returned to their respective hometowns, and the difference in the dates they returned to Hollywood to continue working was only ten days. Similarly, when they came back, they would only shoot two films.

The stories of Irene Dunne and John Boles are as similar as can be. They are both in their early thirties, both born in southern Pennsylvania, and both from ordinary families. They both learned singing and dancing at the same time, and both have very good voices, but their voices were not valued by producers and were assigned to supporting roles in dramas. They entered the film industry almost at the same time.

Although their experiences were very similar, they did not know each other until they co-starred in "Back Street." They have each been married once, and to this day, there has never been any talk of divorce in their respective families. Their hobbies are books and music. Their tastes are the same. Irene Dunne is a famous cook in Hollywood, but surprisingly, John Boles is also a famous chef!

Wallace Beery and the late Marie Dressler's appearance, style, etc., can be said to be as similar as can be. They are so similar that there is no need to compare them further. They both became famous after they gained weight and were over forty years old. Both went from comical, minor roles to becoming leading, older characters. In short, they are similar in every way. In terms of appearance, if you change Marie into men's clothing, she would be Wallace; if you change Wallace into women's clothing, he would be Marie. Their kind personalities and charitable behavior are also equally praised.

The remaining pairs of similar male and female stars cannot be described in detail here, but mentioning their names is enough. One pair is Barbara La Marr and Rudolph Valentino. They were born and died at the same time. One pair is Marjorie Evans and Phillips Holmes. One pair is James Cagney and Joan Blondell. And another pair is William Powell and Katharine Hepburn. Please readers note the similarities between them.

Film Review

Review of "The Merry King"

— Hua Lun

All The King's Horses

— Grand Theatre Showing —

It is no coincidence that the makers of general song and dance films always like to cast the main characters in their films as kings, feudal lords, and other nobles, and set the background in palaces, villas, and fortresses. The main reason is that the players of waltz tunes and the objects they serve are all wealthy and leisured classes. Therefore, in order to cater to their tastes and achieve their business goals, the makers of these films rarely choose emperors, dukes, and other figures as the protagonists of the plays. The background that follows is naturally where they live, eat, drink, and play. At the same time, because these films are due to fiction and clumsy lies, the content is often empty. Therefore, they have to use gorgeous backgrounds and dazzling props to try to cover up or confuse people's attention. Therefore, the palaces of the rich and prominent are the most suitable to be used, and the characters that follow are their masters, the nobles. As for the emperor being amorous and the empress being sentimental, these specific personalities are naturally for the convenience of their stories, which cater to the tastes of the wealthy and leisured who like to be amorous and sentimental.

"The Merry King" is the best illustration of the above.

The story is about a King Rudolf who is so busy with state affairs that he has no time to enjoy the pleasures of the palace. Secondly, in accordance with the custom that kings must have beards, he is troubled and inconvenient to kiss and be intimate. Therefore, Queen Irene angrily moves to the summer palace and does not return for years. The emperor is anxious and asks Carlo, a handsome young man and movie star who has won the love of countless girls, for advice on how to make the queen change her mind. The result is that he shaves his beard, lets Carlo act as his representative, and goes to Vienna to have fun and have an affair with a woman named Mimi.

And this Carlo, the fake emperor who looks like Rudolf, causes many jokes in the parliament and in the harem. The queen hears that the emperor has shaved his beard and rushes back to the palace that night, restoring her true love to the fake emperor. The play unfolds in this way. The story is that Carlo, in order to respect the emperor's reputation, uses various methods to avoid "that," thus completing and restoring the old harmony between the emperor and empress.

Such a fictional story has nothing outstanding in terms of screenwriting. The movie star suddenly becomes the king, and even the queen cannot recognize him. This lie is not technical enough and breaks all previous records. Carlo and the queen are dancing happily, and suddenly Rudolf replaces him. She does not even notice it. Also, the king is so busy that he does not have time to accompany the queen, but he can accompany Carlo to sing while playing the piano. This contradiction is also ridiculous enough.

Looking at it from the performance side, the director Frank Tuttle is quite attentive and has achieved considerable results. First of all, the editing is concise and the tone is cheerful. The liveliness of several camera shots is commendable. Second, he is able to put effort into small actions. For example, the first scene shows the queen's loneliness in the palace. She uses flipping through books, stroking the dog, and making shadows on the wall behind the light to pass the time. Only the movement of her hands can explain her mood. The expression when she hears someone knocking on the door and hurriedly dresses up, thinking that the emperor is coming, and the melancholy when she dances alone with the statue in the summer palace all well explain her inner feelings, paving the way for the passionate mood of singing by the window and dancing in the pavilion later.

Several songs and performances are not much different from other films of this type.

Speaking of acting, Carl Brisson plays two roles, the king and the movie star, but in this play, which does not focus on individuality, both are only performed mediocrely. Relatively speaking, Mary Ellis's queen is performed more deeply and thoughtfully.

The performance of Jieshimalis and Weiqini Boluosi in the medical science blockbuster "Deadlock" will be shown in Nanjing today for the fourth time.

Amazing Scientific Invention: Spinal Anesthesia

The most complex and dangerous event in surgery is the implementation of the operation. Because the life and death of the patient are all hanging in the hands of the surgeon. The urgency of time, the tension of space, and the highest performance of mind and strength are probably fully displayed in this kind of performance. Therefore, doctors dissect the microscopic, compete for the slightest difference, and fight against time, space, and death to regain the most precious and valuable life of mankind. It is indeed necessary to have a steel-like strong wrist and a light-like swift brain. The difficulty of the so-called million-dollar hands can be seen here. But in "Deadlock," starring Jieshimalis, which is currently being shown in Nanjing, he not only saved many lives, but also personally directed the operation, even curing his own incurable disease of having a hole in his abdomen and chest. The spinal anesthesia used and the corrupt content of the medical scum are worth the great attention of the community. In particular, the great star Jieshimalis, who is famous for his strong and powerful personal performances, this is his most proud work since "Waterloo Bridge." The heroine Weiqini Boluosi (Virginia Bruce) (Note: Weiqini is the wife of Joan Gilbert. She has been retired from the film industry for a long time after marriage. This time she made a comeback in "The Sale of Savage Heads" and played a singer, and she is still praised by fans. It goes without saying.

Carl Brisson's New Film, Full of Talent and Artistry

— Man Man

Carl Brisson was originally a popular singer on the European stage. He was recruited by Paramount to Hollywood and starred in "Murder at the Vanities." After its release, it won the enthusiastic welcome of millions of fans. In particular, the song "Cocktails For Two" is still popular in the United States.

Brisson has a gentle and elegant manner, and like Ramon Novarro, he seems to be a typical talent, that is, what we call a "handsome young man." Who would believe that he is also a boxer? But, in fact, he does have a study of boxing. Although he has never formally fought in a ring in Europe, his reputation for being good at boxing is not less than his reputation as a singer. German Crown Prince Wilhelm once learned boxing from him. After he arrived in Hollywood, no matter how busy he was with filming, he always had to spar with the boxer he brought with him for one or two rounds every day. He can really be regarded as a loyal believer in the boxing world.

Recently, he starred in a song and dance film called "Two Hearts in Waltz Time" in London. Whether this film will be shipped to China for release in the future, we can only wait and see.

Another Literary Film: Dickens' Last Work "The Mystery of Edwin Drood"

— Dai

This year, literary films are really in their prime. In the past month alone, quite a few literary films have been shown in Shanghai. Charles Dickens' "A Christmas Carol" was shown at the Nanjing Grand Theatre not long ago, but Dickens' "The Mystery of Edwin Drood" has been filmed by Universal and will meet us at the Grand Shanghai.

Charles Dickens (1812-1870) was a famous British novelist. In his early years, his life was very difficult. He relied entirely on his own strength to become a famous writer. For this reason, he wrote mostly about his own experiences and was known for his descriptions of the lower and middle classes of society. He wrote many works throughout his life, and quite a few have recently been adapted into films by Hollywood film companies.

"The Mystery of Edwin Drood" was the last novel he wrote in 1870, but unfortunately, he passed away before he could finish it. The story is about a clergyman who is highly trusted in society, but his private life is marred by the bad habit of smoking opium. One Christmas Eve, his nephew suddenly disappears during a storm. But everyone knows that the young man's disappearance was due to his rival in love murdering him. It took a lot of trouble to uncover this secret case. Although it is a detective-style film, there are also quite a few jokes in it!

In terms of actors, Claude Rains, who starred in "The Passing of the Third Floor Back," plays the leading role. The story is very suitable for Rains, so his performance allows him to fully display his talent. After Rains starred in "The Passing of the Third Floor Back," American film audiences said that he had the potential to win the Academy Award for Best Actor in 1934. Although he lost, his art has been making rapid progress in recent years, which we cannot deny.

Movie Novel

Living on Velvet (Part Six)

— Ti Yun

Aimeé looked surprised and wanted to ask Thorley what he was doing. Thorley said with a gun, "I want to build an airplane hangar. I want to do business." Aimeé said, "What do you want to do?" Thorley said again, "I want to do business. Listen to me. I want to buy an airplane... a seaplane. I can carry the people living in the countryside here to and from the city and the countryside... I can park it in the river, right at the mouth of the waterfront street. It takes them an hour and a half by train, but it only takes them fifteen minutes by plane. This is guaranteed to make money. Of course, I'm afraid I'll lose some money in the first year. But it's guaranteed to make money in the future... Besides, I can go to the sky again!"

Aimeé said, "Thorley, how much does that plane... cost?" Thorley took a pencil from his pocket, picked up an old envelope, and started calculating. He said, "Of course... the cost is more than just the price of the plane... I also need to rent more land... to level it... to build a hangar... workers... equipment... In addition, there is also the salary of your airfield manager, etc.... I hope you will also forgive me for not being able to pay a large salary."

As he spoke, he looked up at Aimeé, but Aimeé remained silent, as if she did not approve. So Thorley continued, "Calculating like this, the total is ten thousand one hundred seventy-one dollars and sixty-seven cents. Don't be stunned like that, Aimeé. After we pay the bills and buy things, we still have eight thousand dollars... Let's think of a way to get two thousand dollars more, and that's not a difficult thing..."

He did build an airplane hangar and bought an airplane. One sunny afternoon, Aimeé performed a naming ceremony for it with a bottle of persimmon jam. After this simple and pitiful ceremony was over, Thorley got on the plane himself, wanting to fly around with Aimeé in the sky, but Aimeé refused.

"I'll go alone," Thorley said. "I'll be down in a minute... about ten minutes will be enough." His face showed impatience, eager to compare himself with the sky. That had become his nature. Aimeé had no choice but to agree, "Go ahead."

Thorley flew alone in the sky for a while and then came down. But when he returned home, he saw Aimeé wearing her going-out clothes, sitting on a large leather bag. He stopped, looked at her, and asked her what she was doing. Aimeé said simply, "I'm leaving you." Thorley said, "Take off those clothes, it's time to prepare dinner now." He forced a smile, but Aimeé said seriously, "Before I leave, I want to say something to you. Your attitude towards life and the world is really too difficult. I know you have a void in your life, a very obvious and terrible void. When I married you, I thought I could fill that void... but I didn't. I'm no longer worthy to be your wife."

Thorley shook his head slightly and said, "You really know how to talk, but... you can't leave. You... you can't deprive me of my life. I think you're a very good wife... really." Aimeé's eyes were full of tears. She said, "I wanted to be able to help you, but I couldn't help you... Alas, Thorley... because I love you so much... I can't help but leave you." Thorley pleaded, "Hate me if you want, but please don't go. Listen to me, Aimeé... I love you... I love you... (To be continued)
